class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Example.of.complex.text.rendering.svg/80px-Example.of.complex.text.rendering.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">You may need <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Indic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Indic)">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Brahmic_scripts" title="Brahmic scripts">Indic text</a> in this article correctly.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sri Lanka</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span></span> <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="/&#331;/: \'ng\' in \'sing\'">&#331;</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>, <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#643;/: \'sh\' in \'shy\'">&#643;</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/i&#720;/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i&#720;</span></span> <wbr/>-/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/- <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="/&#331;/: \'ng\' in \'sing\'">&#331;</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Sri_Lanka.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/En-us-Sri_Lanka.ogg" title="En-us-Sri Lanka.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" title="Sinhalese language">Sinhalese</a>: <span lang="si">&#3521;&#3530;&#8205;&#3515;&#3539; &#3517;&#3458;&#3482;&#3535;</span> <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit transliteration">&#346;r&#299; La&#7747;k&#257;</i></i>; <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>: <span lang="ta">&#2951;&#2994;&#2969;&#3021;&#2965;&#3016;</span> <i>Ila&#7749;kai</i>), officially the <b>Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> to the southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> and to the southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a>. The island is historically and culturally intertwined  with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, but is geographically separated from the Indian subcontinent by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mannar" title="Gulf of Mannar">Gulf of Mannar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palk_Strait" title="Palk Strait">Palk Strait</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">legislative capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Jayawardenepura_Kotte" title="Sri Jayawardenepura Kotte">Sri Jayawardenepura Kotte</a>, is a suburb of the commercial capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>.\n</p><p>Sri Lanka\'s documented history spans 3,000 years, with evidence of pre-historic human settlements dating back to at least 125,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-histr_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-histr-13">[13]</a></sup> It has a rich cultural heritage and the first known <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Buddhism in Sri Lanka">Buddhist</a> writings of Sri Lanka, the <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="P&#257;li Canon">P&#257;li Canon</a>, date back to the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Buddhist_council" title="Fourth Buddhist council">Fourth Buddhist council</a> in 29 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Its geographic location and deep harbours made it of great strategic importance from the time of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> through to the modern <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Silk_Road" title="Maritime Silk Road">Maritime Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silkr_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-silkr-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka was known from the <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">beginning of British colonial rule</a> as <b>Ceylon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#594;/: \'o\' in \'body\'">&#594;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span style="font-size:85%;">US also</span> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="/e&#618;/: \'a\' in \'face\'">e&#618;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#594;/: \'o\' in \'body\'">&#594;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>). A nationalist political movement arose in the country in the early 20th century to obtain political independence, which was granted in 1948; the country became a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> and adopted its current name in 1972. Sri Lanka\'s recent history has been marred by a 30-year <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Sri Lankan Civil War">civil war</a>, which decisively ended when the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lanka Armed Forces</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam" title="Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam">Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam</a> (LTTE) in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current constitution stipulates the political system as a republic and a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> governed by a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a>. It has had a long history of international engagement, as a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (SAARC), and a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">G77</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, Sri Lanka is one of only two South Asian countries rated "high" on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), with its HDI rating and <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> the highest among South Asian nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDI_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-10">[10]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan constitution accords <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> the "foremost place", although it does not identify it as a <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>. Buddhism is given special privileges in the Sri Lankan constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island is home to many cultures, languages and ethnicities. The majority of the population is from the <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_people" title="Sinhalese people">Sinhalese ethnicity</a>, while a large minority of <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamils</a> have also played an influential role in the island\'s history. <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Moors" title="Sri Lankan Moors">Moors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burghers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Malays" title="Sri Lankan Malays">Malays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Chinese people in Sri Lanka">Chinese</a>, and the indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedda_people" title="Vedda people">Vedda</a> are also established groups on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" divisions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Foreign_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Foreign relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Military"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Urban_centres"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Urban centres</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Human_rights_and_media"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Human rights and media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Food_and_festivals"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Food and festivals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Visual,_literary_and_performing_arts"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Visual, literary and performing arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Names of Sri Lanka">Names of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>In antiquity, Sri Lanka was known to travellers by a variety of names. According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Mahavamsa" title="Mahavamsa">Mahavamsa</a></i>, the legendary <a href="/wiki/Prince_Vijaya" title="Prince Vijaya">Prince Vijaya</a> named the land <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tambapanni" title="Kingdom of Tambapanni">Tambapanni</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copper_red" title="Copper red">copper-red</a> hands" or "copper-red earth"), because his followers\' hands were reddened by the <a href="/wiki/Red_soil" title="Red soil">red soil</a> of the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMS_1997_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMS_1997-23">[23]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a>, such as the Ramayana, the island was referred to as <a href="/wiki/Lanka" title="Lanka"><i>Lank&#257;</i></a> ("Island"). The Tamil term <a href="/wiki/Eelam" title="Eelam">Eelam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>: <span lang="ta">&#2952;&#2996;&#2990;&#3021;</span>, <small><abbr title="transliteration">translit.</abbr>&#160;</small><i lang="ta-Latn" title="Tamil-language transliteration">&#299;&#7739;am</i>), was used to designate the whole island in <a href="/wiki/Sangam_literature" title="Sangam literature">Sangam literature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ancient Greek geographers called it <i><a href="/wiki/Taprobana" title="Taprobana">Taproban&#257;</a></i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">&#932;&#945;&#960;&#961;&#959;&#946;&#945;&#957;&#8118;</span>) or <i>Taproban&#275;</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#932;&#945;&#960;&#961;&#959;&#946;&#945;&#957;&#8134;</span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> from the word <i>Tambapanni</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> referred to it as <i>Sarand&#299;b</i> (the origin of the word "<a href="/wiki/Serendipity" title="Serendipity">serendipity</a>") from <i>Cerentivu</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> or <i>Si&#7747;haladv&#299;pa&#7717;</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Ceylon" title="Portuguese Ceylon">Ceil&#227;o</a></i>, the name given to Sri Lanka by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> when it arrived in 1505,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> was transliterated into English as <i>Ceylon</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a>, the island was known as <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">Ceylon</a>; it achieved independence as the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Dominion of Ceylon</a> in 1948.\n</p><p>The country is now known in Sinhalese as <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit transliteration">&#346;r&#299; La&#7747;k&#257;</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" title="Sinhalese language">Sinhalese</a>: <span lang="si">&#3521;&#3530;&#8205;&#3515;&#3539; &#3517;&#3458;&#3482;&#3535;</span>) and in Tamil as <i><i lang="sa-Latn" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit transliteration">Ila&#7749;kai</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>: <span lang="ta">&#2951;&#2994;&#2969;&#3021;&#2965;&#3016;</span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Tamil" title="Help:IPA/Tamil">[i&#712;la&#331;&#609;ai]</a></span>). In 1972, its formal name was changed to "Free, Sovereign and Independent Republic of Sri Lanka". Later in 1978 it was changed to the "Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> As the name Ceylon still appears in the names of a number of organisations, the Sri Lankan government announced in 2011 a plan to rename all those over which it has authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sri_Lanka" title="History of Sri Lanka">History of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Prehistory of Sri Lanka">Prehistory of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>The pre-history of Sri Lanka goes back 125,000 years and possibly even as far back as 500,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pps_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-pps-34">[34]</a></sup> The era spans the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palaeolithic" title="Palaeolithic">Palaeolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Ages</a>. Among the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> human settlements discovered in Sri Lanka, <a href="/wiki/Fa_Hien_Cave" title="Fa Hien Cave">Pahiyangala</a> (named after the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> traveller <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">monk</a> <a href="/wiki/Faxian" title="Faxian">Faxian</a>), which dates back to 37,000 BP,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Batadombalena" title="Batadombalena">Batadombalena</a> (28,500 BP)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-btd_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-btd-36">[36]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Belilena" title="Belilena">Belilena</a> (12,000 BP) are the most important. In these caves, archaeologists have found the remains of <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">anatomically</a> modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humans" title="Humans">humans</a> which they have named <a href="/wiki/Balangoda_Man" title="Balangoda Man">Balangoda Man</a>, and other evidence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> suggesting that they may have engaged in <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and kept domestic dogs for driving game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the first written references to the island is found in the Indian <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, which provides details of a kingdom named <i><a href="/wiki/Lanka" title="Lanka">Lanka</a></i> that was created by the divine sculptor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vishwakarma" title="Vishwakarma">Vishwakarma</a> for <a href="/wiki/Kubera" title="Kubera">Kubera</a>, the Lord of Wealth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> It is said that Kubera was overthrown by his demon stepbrother <a href="/wiki/Ravana" title="Ravana">Ravana</a>, the powerful emperor who built a mythical <a href="/wiki/Early_flying_machines" title="Early flying machines">flying machine</a> named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dandu_Monara" title="Dandu Monara">Dandu Monara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parkrsl_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-parkrsl-40">[40]</a></sup> The modern city of <a href="/wiki/Wariyapola" title="Wariyapola">Wariyapola</a> is described as Ravana\'s airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Early inhabitants of Sri Lanka were probably ancestors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedda_people" title="Vedda people">Vedda people</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> an indigenous people numbering approximately 2,500 living in modern-day Sri Lanka. The 19th-century Irish historian <a href="/wiki/James_Emerson_Tennent" title="James Emerson Tennent">James Emerson Tennent</a> theorized that <a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a>, a city in southern Sri Lanka, was the ancient seaport of <a href="/wiki/Tarshish" title="Tarshish">Tarshish</a> from which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Solomon" title="King Solomon">King Solomon</a> is said to have drawn <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peafowl" title="Peafowl">peacocks</a>, and other valuables.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Anuradhapura_period">Pre-Anuradhapura period</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_kingdoms_period" title="Early kingdoms period">Early kingdoms period</a></div>\n<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Mahavamsa" title="Mahavamsa">Mah&#257;vamsa</a></i>, a chronicle written in <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">P&#257;&#7735;i</a>, the original inhabitants of Sri Lanka are the <a href="/wiki/Yaksha" title="Yaksha">Yakshas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naga_people_(Lanka)" title="Naga people (Lanka)">Nagas</a>. Ancient cemeteries that were used before 600 <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">BC</a> and other signs of advanced civilization have also been discovered in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Sinhalese history traditionally starts in 543 BC with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Vijaya" title="Prince Vijaya">Prince Vijaya</a>, a semi-legendary prince who sailed with 700 followers to Sri Lanka, after being expelled from <a href="/wiki/Vanga_Kingdom" title="Vanga Kingdom">Vanga Kingdom</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> He established the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tambapanni" title="Kingdom of Tambapanni">Kingdom of Tambapanni</a>, near modern-day <a href="/wiki/Mannar,_Sri_Lanka" title="Mannar, Sri Lanka">Mannar</a>. Vijaya (Singha) is the first of the approximately 189 native <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarchs</a> of Sri Lanka described in chronicles such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Dipavamsa" title="Dipavamsa">Dipavamsa</a></i>, <i>Mah&#257;va&#7747;sa</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Culavamsa" title="Culavamsa">C&#363;&#7735;ava&#7747;sa</a></i>, and <i>R&#257;j&#257;valiya</i> (<i>see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Sinhalese_monarchs" title="List of Sinhalese monarchs">list of Sinhalese monarchs</a></i>). Sri Lankan dynastic history ended in 1815, when the island became part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anuradhapura_period">Anuradhapura period</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anuradhapura_period" title="Anuradhapura period">Anuradhapura period</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3429" data-file-width="5143" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg/250px-Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg/375px-Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg/500px-Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buda_de_Avukana_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Avukana_Buddha_statue" title="Avukana Buddha statue">Avukana Buddha statue</a>, a 12 metres (39&#160;ft) tall standing Buddha statue from the reign of <a href="/wiki/Dhatusena_of_Anuradhapura" title="Dhatusena of Anuradhapura">Dhatusena of Anuradhapura</a>, 5th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Anuradhapura_Kingdom" title="Anuradhapura Kingdom">Anuradhapura Kingdom</a> was established in 380 BC during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Pandukabhaya_of_Anuradhapura" title="Pandukabhaya of Anuradhapura">Pandukabhaya of Anuradhapura</a>. Thereafter, Anuradhapura served as the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> of the country for nearly 1,400 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Ancient Sri Lankans excelled at building certain types of structures (<a href="/wiki/Ancient_constructions_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Ancient constructions of Sri Lanka">constructions</a>) such as <a href="/wiki/Irrigation_works_in_ancient_Sri_Lanka" title="Irrigation works in ancient Sri Lanka">tanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">dagobas</a> and palaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Society underwent a major transformation during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Devanampiya_Tissa_of_Anuradhapura" title="Devanampiya Tissa of Anuradhapura">Devanampiya Tissa of Anuradhapura</a>, with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> from India. In 250 BC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mahinda_(Buddhist_monk)" title="Mahinda (Buddhist monk)">Mahinda</a>, the son of the <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">Mauryan</a> Emperor <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">bhikkhu</a> (Buddhist monk) arrived in <a href="/wiki/Mihintale" title="Mihintale">Mihintale</a> carrying the message of Buddhism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macmillan1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macmillan1-49">[49]</a></sup> His mission won over the monarch, who embraced the faith and propagated it throughout the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinhala_people" title="Sinhala people">Sinhalese population</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahav1_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-mahav1-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Succeeding kingdoms of Sri Lanka would maintain a large number of <a href="/wiki/Schools_of_Buddhism" title="Schools of Buddhism">Buddhist schools</a> and monasteries and support the propagation of Buddhism into other countries in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. Sri Lankan Bhikkhus studied in India\'s famous ancient Buddhist University of <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nalanda</a>, which was destroyed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Bakhtiyar_Khilji" title="Muhammad bin Bakhtiyar Khilji">Bakhtiyar Khilji</a>. It is probable that many of the scriptures from Nalanda are preserved in Sri Lanka\'s many monasteries and that the written form of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tipitaka" title="Tipitaka">Tipitaka</a>, including Sinhalese Buddhist literature, were part of the University of Nalanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 245 BC, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhikkhuni" title="Bhikkhuni">bhikkhuni</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangamitta" title="Sangamitta">Sangamitta</a> arrived with the <a href="/wiki/Jaya_Sri_Maha_Bodhi" title="Jaya Sri Maha Bodhi">Jaya Sri Maha Bodhi</a> tree, which is considered to be a sapling from the historical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bodhi_tree" title="Bodhi tree">Bodhi tree</a> under which <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Gautama Buddha</a> became enlightened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> It is considered the oldest human-planted tree (with a continuous historical record) in the world. (<a href="/wiki/Bodhi_Vamsa" title="Bodhi Vamsa">Bodhivamsa</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Invasions</dt></dl>\n<p>Sri Lanka first experienced a foreign invasion during the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suratissa_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Suratissa of Sri Lanka">Suratissa</a>, who was defeated by two horse traders named <a href="/wiki/Sena_and_Guttika" title="Sena and Guttika">Sena and Guttika</a> from <a href="/wiki/South_India" title="South India">South India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mahav1_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-mahav1-50">[50]</a></sup> The next invasion came immediately in 205 BC by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chola" title="Chola">Chola</a> king named <a href="/wiki/Ellalan" title="Ellalan">Ellalan</a>, who overthrew <a href="/wiki/Asela_of_Anuradhapura" title="Asela of Anuradhapura">Asela</a> and ruled the country for 44 years. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutthagamani_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Dutthagamani of Sri Lanka">Dutugemunu</a>, the eldest son of the southern regional sub-king, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavan_Tissa" title="Kavan Tissa">Kavan Tissa</a>, defeated Elara in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vijithapura" title="Battle of Vijithapura">Battle of Vijithapura</a>. He built <a href="/wiki/Ruwanwelisaya" title="Ruwanwelisaya">Ruwanwelisaya</a>, the second stupa in ancient Sri Lanka, and the <a href="/wiki/Lovamahapaya" title="Lovamahapaya">Lovamahapaya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During its two and a half millennia of existence, the Kingdom of Sri Lanka was invaded at least eight times by neighbouring South Asian dynasties such as the <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Chola</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pandya_dynasty" title="Pandya dynasty">Pandya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chera_dynasty" title="Chera dynasty">Chera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pallava_dynasty" title="Pallava dynasty">Pallava</a>. These invaders were all subsequently driven back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> There also were incursions by the kingdoms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalinga_(historical_kingdom)" title="Kalinga (historical kingdom)">Kalinga</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a>) and from the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> as well. <i><a href="/wiki/Kala_Wewa" title="Kala Wewa">Kala Wewa</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Avukana_Buddha_statue" title="Avukana Buddha statue">Avukana Buddha statue</a> were built during the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhatusena_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Dhatusena of Sri Lanka">Dhatusena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sarachchandra_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-sarachchandra-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Fourth Buddhist Council</dt></dl>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Buddhist_council" title="Fourth Buddhist council">Fourth Buddhist council</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg/220px-Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg/330px-Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg/440px-Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Temple_of_Dambulla-111107.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sculpture of reclining Buddha at <a href="/wiki/Dambulla_cave_temple" title="Dambulla cave temple">Dambulla cave temple</a>, declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1991</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1426" data-file-width="2094" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg/220px-Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg/330px-Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg/440px-Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ptolemy%27s_Taprobana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ptolemy%27s_world_map" title="Ptolemy\'s world map">Ptolemy\'s world map</a> of Ceylon, first century AD, in a 1535 publication</div></div></div>\n<p>The Fourth Buddhist council of <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada Buddhism</a> was held at the <a href="/wiki/Anuradhapura_Maha_Viharaya" title="Anuradhapura Maha Viharaya">Anuradhapura Maha Viharaya</a> in Sri Lanka under the patronage of <a href="/wiki/Valagamba_of_Anuradhapura" title="Valagamba of Anuradhapura">Valagamba of Anuradhapura</a> in 25 BC. The council was held in response to a year in which the harvests in Sri Lanka were particularly poor and many <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">Buddhist monks</a> subsequently died of starvation. Because the <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="P&#257;li Canon">P&#257;li Canon</a> was at that time <a href="/wiki/Oral_literature" title="Oral literature">oral literature</a> maintained in several recensions by <i>dhammabh&#257;&#7751;aka</i>s (<a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">dharma</a> reciters), the surviving monks recognized the danger of not writing it down so that even if some of the monks whose duty it was to study and remember parts of the Canon for later generations died, the teachings would not be lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELopez2013200_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELopez2013200-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Council, <a href="/wiki/Palm-leaf_manuscript" title="Palm-leaf manuscript">palm-leaf manuscripts</a> containing the completed Canon were taken to other countries such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Later periods</dt></dl>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sigiriya.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sigiriya.jpg/220px-Sigiriya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sigiriya.jpg/330px-Sigiriya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sigiriya.jpg/440px-Sigiriya.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sigiriya.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sigiriya" title="Sigiriya">Sigiriya</a> rock fortress</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sigiriya_ladies.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sigiriya_ladies.jpg/220px-Sigiriya_ladies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sigiriya_ladies.jpg/330px-Sigiriya_ladies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sigiriya_ladies.jpg/440px-Sigiriya_ladies.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sigiriya_ladies.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sigiriya#Frescoes" title="Sigiriya">Frescoes on the Sigiriya</a> rock fortress in <a href="/wiki/Matale_District" title="Matale District">Matale District</a>, 5th century</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka was the first Asian country known to have a female ruler: <a href="/wiki/Anula_of_Anuradhapura" title="Anula of Anuradhapura">Anula of Anuradhapura</a> (r. 47&#8211;42 BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sigiriya12_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-sigiriya12-58">[58]</a></sup> Sri Lankan monarchs undertook some remarkable construction projects such as <a href="/wiki/Sigiriya" title="Sigiriya">Sigiriya</a>, the so-called "Fortress in the Sky", built during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Kashyapa_I_of_Anuradhapura" title="Kashyapa I of Anuradhapura">Kashyapa I of Anuradhapura</a>, who ruled between 477 and 495. The Sigiriya rock fortress is surrounded by an extensive network of ramparts and moats. Inside this protective enclosure were gardens, ponds, pavilions, palaces and other structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponnamperuma_2013_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ponnamperuma_2013-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bandaranayake_1999_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bandaranayake_1999-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1,600-year-old Sigiriya frescoes are an example of ancient Sri Lankan art at its finest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponnamperuma_2013_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ponnamperuma_2013-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bandaranayake_1999_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bandaranayake_1999-60">[60]</a></sup> They are one of the best preserved examples of ancient urban planning in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-61">[61]</a></sup> They have been declared by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as one of the seven World Heritage Sites in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Among other structures, large <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">reservoirs</a>, important for conserving water in a climate with rainy and dry seasons, and elaborate <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(water_supply)" title="Aqueduct (water supply)">aqueducts</a>, some with a slope as finely calibrated as one inch to the mile, are most notable. Biso Kotuwa, a peculiar construction inside a <a href="/wiki/Dam" title="Dam">dam</a>, is a technological marvel based on precise <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> that allows water to flow outside the dam, keeping pressure on the dam to a minimum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ancient Sri Lanka was the first country in the world to establish a dedicated hospital, in <a href="/wiki/Mihintale" title="Mihintale">Mihintale</a> in the 4th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> It was also the leading exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a> in the ancient world. It maintained close ties with European civilisations including the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. For example, Bhatikabhaya (22 BC &#8211; AD 7) sent an envoy to Rome who brought back <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_coral" title="Red coral">red coral</a>, which was used to make an elaborate netlike adornment for the <a href="/wiki/Ruwanwelisaya" title="Ruwanwelisaya">Ruwanwelisaya</a>. In addition, Sri Lankan male dancers witnessed the assassination of Caligula. When Queen Cleopatra sent her son <a href="/wiki/Caesarion" title="Caesarion">Caesarion</a> into hiding, he was headed to Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-got_down_coral_for_a_net_explained_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-got_down_coral_for_a_net_explained-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fli_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-fli-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Upasampada" title="Upasampada">upasampada</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhikkhuni" title="Bhikkhuni">bhikkhunis</a> (Buddhist nuns) first arrived in China when Devas&#257;ra and ten other bhikkhunis came from Sri Lanka at the request of Chinese women and established the order there in 429.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaung_Paw7_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaung_Paw7-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polonnaruwa_and_transitional_periods">Polonnaruwa and transitional periods</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Polonnaruwa_period" title="Polonnaruwa period">Polonnaruwa period</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transitional_period_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Transitional period of Sri Lanka">Transitional period of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>The medieval period of Sri Lanka begins with the fall of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Anuradhapura" title="Kingdom of Anuradhapura">Anuradhapura Kingdom</a>. In AD 993, the invasion of <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Chola emperor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajaraja_I" title="Rajaraja I">Rajaraja I</a> forced the then Sri Lankan ruler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahinda_V_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Mahinda V of Sri Lanka">Mahinda V</a> to flee to the southern part of Sri Lanka. Taking advantage of this situation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajendra_I" title="Rajendra I">Rajendra I</a>, son of Rajaraja I, launched a large invasion in 1017. Mahinda V was captured and taken to India, and the Cholas <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chola_occupation_of_Sri_Lanka_(993-1077)" title="Chola occupation of Sri Lanka (993-1077)">sacked the city of Anuradhapura</a>. Subsequently, they moved the capital to <a href="/wiki/Polonnaruwa" title="Polonnaruwa">Polonnaruwa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Siriweera_2004,_p._44_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Siriweera_2004,_p._44-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This marked the end of the two great dynasties of ancient Sri Lanka, the Moriya and the Lambakanna. Following a seventeen-year-long campaign, <a href="/wiki/Vijayabahu_I_of_Polonnaruwa" title="Vijayabahu I of Polonnaruwa">Vijayabahu I</a> successfully drove the Chola out of Sri Lanka in 1070, reuniting the country for the first time in over a century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Upon his request, ordained monks were sent from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a> to Sri Lanka to re-establish Buddhism, which had almost disappeared from the country during the Chola reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> During the medieval period, Sri Lanka was divided into three sub-territories, namely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ruhuna" title="Kingdom of Ruhuna">Ruhunu</a>, Pihiti and <a href="/wiki/Maya_Rata" title="Maya Rata">Maya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_(pixinn.net).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="810" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/170px-SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/255px-SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/340px-SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SriLanka_BuddhistStatue_(pixinn.net).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Buddhist statue in the ancient capital city of <a href="/wiki/Polonnaruwa" title="Polonnaruwa">Polonnaruwa</a>, 12th century</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka\'s <a href="/wiki/Irrigation_works_in_ancient_Sri_Lanka" title="Irrigation works in ancient Sri Lanka">irrigation system</a> was extensively expanded during the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parakramabahu_I_of_Polonnaruwa" title="Parakramabahu I of Polonnaruwa">Par&#257;kramab&#257;hu the Great</a> (1153&#8211;1186).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethniccr_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ethniccr-73">[73]</a></sup> This period is considered as a time when Sri Lanka was at the height of its power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> He built 1470 reservoirs &#8211; the highest number by any ruler in Sri Lanka\'s history &#8211; repaired 165 dams, 3910 canals, 163 major reservoirs, and 2376 mini-reservoirs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethniccr1_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-ethniccr1-76">[76]</a></sup> His most famous construction is the <a href="/wiki/Parakrama_Samudra" title="Parakrama Samudra">Parakrama Samudra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> the largest irrigation project of medieval Sri Lanka. Par&#257;kramab&#257;hu\'s reign is memorable for two major campaigns &#8211; in the south of India as part of a Pandyan war of succession, and a punitive strike against the kings of Ramanna (<a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>) for various perceived insults to Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After his demise, Sri Lanka gradually decayed in power. In 1215, <a href="/wiki/Kalinga_Magha" title="Kalinga Magha">Kalinga Magha</a>, a South Indian with uncertain origins, identified as the founder of the Jaffna kingdom, invaded and captured the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Polonnaruwa" title="Kingdom of Polonnaruwa">Kingdom of Polonnaruwa</a>. He sailed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalinga_(historical_kingdom)" title="Kalinga (historical kingdom)">Kalinga</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethniccr1_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-ethniccr1-76">[76]</a></sup> 690 nautical miles on 100 large ships with a 24,000 strong army. Unlike previous invaders, he <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looted</a>, ransacked, and destroyed everything in the ancient Anuradhapura and Polonnaruwa Kingdoms beyond recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> His priorities in ruling were to extract as much as possible from the land and overturn as many of the traditions of <a href="/wiki/Rajarata" title="Rajarata">Rajarata</a> as possible. His reign saw the massive migration of native <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_people" title="Sinhalese people">Sinhalese people</a> to the south and west of Sri Lanka, and into the mountainous interior, in a bid to escape his power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nadarajan,_V_p._72_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nadarajan,_V_p._72-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indrapala,_K_p._16_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indrapala,_K_p._16-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka never really recovered from the impact of Kalinga Magha\'s invasion. King Vijayab&#226;hu III, who led the resistance, brought the kingdom to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dambadeniya" title="Kingdom of Dambadeniya">Dambadeniya</a>. The north, in the meanwhile, eventually evolved into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaffna_kingdom" title="Jaffna kingdom">Jaffna kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nadarajan,_V_p._72_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nadarajan,_V_p._72-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indrapala,_K_p._16_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Indrapala,_K_p._16-81">[81]</a></sup> The Jaffna kingdom never came under the rule of any kingdom of the south except on one occasion; in 1450, following the conquest led by king <a href="/wiki/Parakramabahu_VI_of_Kotte" title="Parakramabahu VI of Kotte">Par&#226;kramab&#226;hu VI</a>\'s adopted son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhuvanekabahu_VI_of_Kotte" title="Bhuvanekabahu VI of Kotte">Prince Sapumal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> He ruled the North from AD 1450 to 1467.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next three centuries starting from 1215 were marked by kaleidoscopically shifting collections of kingdoms in south and central Sri Lanka, including Dambadeniya, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dambadeniya_from_Yapahuwa" title="Kingdom of Dambadeniya from Yapahuwa">Yapahuwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gampola" title="Gampola">Gampola</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Raigama" title="Kingdom of Raigama">Raigama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kotte" title="Kingdom of Kotte">Kotte</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HC_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-HC-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sitawaka" title="Kingdom of Sitawaka">Sitawaka</a>, and finally, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kandy" title="Kingdom of Kandy">Kandy</a>. Chinese admiral <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a> and his naval expeditionary force landed at Galle, Sri Lanka in 1409 and got into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming-Kotte_War" title="Ming-Kotte War">battle</a> with the local king <a href="/wiki/Vira_Alakesvara_of_Gampola" title="Vira Alakesvara of Gampola">Vira Alakesvara of Gampola</a>. Zheng He captured King Vira Alakesvara and later released him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Zheng He erected the <a href="/wiki/Galle_Trilingual_Inscription" title="Galle Trilingual Inscription">Galle Trilingual Inscription</a>, a stone tablet at <a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a> written in three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>), to commemorate his visit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">stele</a> was discovered by S. H. Thomlin at Galle in 1911 and is now preserved in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombo_National_Museum" title="Colombo National Museum">Colombo National Museum</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kandyan_period">Kandyan period</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Ceylon" title="Portuguese Ceylon">Portuguese Ceylon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Dutch Ceylon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpilbergenVimala.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="493" data-file-width="733" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SpilbergenVimala.jpg/220px-SpilbergenVimala.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SpilbergenVimala.jpg/330px-SpilbergenVimala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SpilbergenVimala.jpg/440px-SpilbergenVimala.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpilbergenVimala.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 17th-century painting of Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Joris_van_Spilbergen" title="Joris van Spilbergen">Joris van Spilbergen</a> meeting with King Vimaladharmasuriya in 1602</div></div></div>\n<p>The early modern period of Sri Lanka begins with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> soldier and explorer <a href="/wiki/Louren%C3%A7o_de_Almeida" title="Louren&#231;o de Almeida">Louren&#231;o de Almeida</a>, the son of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida" title="Francisco de Almeida">Francisco de Almeida</a>, in 1505.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-francal_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-francal-91">[91]</a></sup> In 1517, the Portuguese built a fort at the port city of <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a> and gradually extended their control over the coastal areas. In 1592, after decades of intermittent warfare with the Portuguese, <a href="/wiki/Vimaladharmasuriya_I_of_Kandy" title="Vimaladharmasuriya I of Kandy">Vimaladharmasuriya I</a> moved his kingdom to the inland city of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kandy" title="Kingdom of Kandy">Kandy</a>, a location he thought more secure from attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isl23_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-isl23-92">[92]</a></sup> In 1619, succumbing to attacks by the Portuguese, the independent existence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaffna_kingdom" title="Jaffna kingdom">Jaffna kingdom</a> came to an end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the reign of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajasinghe_II_of_Kandy" title="Rajasinghe II of Kandy">Rajasinghe II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> explorers arrived on the island. In 1638, the king signed a <a href="/wiki/Kandyan_Treaty_of_1638" title="Kandyan Treaty of 1638">treaty</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> to get rid of the Portuguese who ruled most of the coastal areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The following <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" title="Dutch&#8211;Portuguese War">Dutch&#8211;Portuguese War</a> resulted in a Dutch victory, with Colombo falling into Dutch hands by 1656. The Dutch remained in the areas they had captured, thereby violating the treaty they had signed in 1638. An ethnic group named <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burgher people</a> emerged in Sri Lankan society as a result of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_period_in_Ceylon" title="Dutch period in Ceylon">Dutch rule</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Kingdom of Kandy was the last independent monarchy of Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kandyk_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-kandyk-96">[96]</a></sup> In 1595, Vimaladharmasurya brought the sacred <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tooth_Relic" title="Tooth Relic">Tooth Relic</a> &#8211; the traditional symbol of royal and religious authority amongst the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinhala_people" title="Sinhala people">Sinhalese</a> &#8211; to Kandy, and built the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Tooth" title="Temple of the Tooth">Temple of the Tooth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kandyk_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-kandyk-96">[96]</a></sup> In spite of on-going intermittent warfare with Europeans, the kingdom survived. Later, a crisis of succession emerged in Kandy upon king <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vira_Narendra_Sinha_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Vira Narendra Sinha of Sri Lanka">Vira Narendrasinha</a>\'s death in 1739. He was married to a <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>-speaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nayaks_of_Madurai" title="Nayaks of Madurai">Nayakkar</a> princess from South India (<a href="/wiki/Madurai" title="Madurai">Madurai</a>) and was childless by her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kandyk_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-kandyk-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eventually, with the support of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhikku" title="Bhikku">bhikku</a> Weliwita Sarankara, the crown passed to the brother of one of Narendrasinha\'s princesses, overlooking the right of <i>"Unambuwe Bandara"</i>, Narendrasinha\'s own son by a Sinhalese <a href="/wiki/Concubinage" title="Concubinage">concubine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The new king was crowned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vijaya_Rajasinha_of_Kandy" title="Vijaya Rajasinha of Kandy">Sri Vijaya Rajasinha</a> later that year. Kings of the Nayakkar dynasty launched several attacks on Dutch controlled areas, which proved to be unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_rule">British rule</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">British Ceylon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="448" data-file-width="288" decoding="async" height="342" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha.jpg/220px-Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha_of_Kandy" title="Sri Vikrama Rajasinha of Kandy">Sri Vikrama Rajasinha of Kandy</a>, the last ruling Sri Lankan monarch</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, fearing that <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> control of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> might deliver Sri Lanka to the French, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> occupied the coastal areas of the island (which they <a href="/wiki/Geographical_renaming" title="Geographical renaming">called</a> Ceylon) with little difficulty in 1796.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colvoyg_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-colvoyg-99">[99]</a></sup> Two years later, in 1798, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Rajadhi_Rajasinha_of_Kandy" title="Sri Rajadhi Rajasinha of Kandy">Sri Rajadhi Rajasinha</a>, third of the four Nayakkar kings of Sri Lanka, died of a fever. Following his death, a nephew of Rajadhi Rajasinha, eighteen-year-old Kannasamy, was crowned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scnsl_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-scnsl-100">[100]</a></sup> The young king, now named <a href="/wiki/Sri_Vikrama_Rajasinha_of_Kandy" title="Sri Vikrama Rajasinha of Kandy">Sri Vikrama Rajasinha</a>, faced a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> invasion in 1803 but successfully retaliated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scnsl_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-scnsl-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By then the entire coastal area was under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">Treaty of Amiens</a>. On 14 February 1815, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kandy" title="Kingdom of Kandy">Kandy</a> was occupied by the British in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kandian_Wars" title="Kandian Wars">second Kandyan War</a>, ending Sri Lanka\'s independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scnsl_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-scnsl-100">[100]</a></sup> Sri Vikrama Rajasinha, the last native monarch of Sri Lanka, was exiled to India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kandyan_Convention" title="Kandyan Convention">Kandyan Convention</a> formally ceded the entire country to the British Empire. Attempts by Sri Lankan noblemen to undermine British power in 1818 during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Rebellion_of_1817-1818" title="Great Rebellion of 1817-1818">Uva Rebellion</a> were thwarted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_governors_of_Ceylon" title="British governors of Ceylon">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Brownrigg" title="Robert Brownrigg">Robert Brownrigg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppetipola_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-keppetipola-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The beginning of the modern period of Sri Lanka is marked by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colebrooke-Cameron_Commission" title="Colebrooke-Cameron Commission">Colebrooke-Cameron reforms</a> of 1833.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corankel_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-corankel-103">[103]</a></sup> They introduced a <a href="/wiki/Utilitarianism" title="Utilitarianism">utilitarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> political culture to the country based on the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> and amalgamated the Kandyan and maritime provinces as a single unit of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corankel_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-corankel-103">[103]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_Ceylon" title="Executive Council of Ceylon">executive council</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_Ceylon" title="Legislative Council of Ceylon">legislative council</a> were established, later becoming the foundation of a representative legislature. By this time, experiments with <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> plantations were largely successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nubin_2002_115_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nubin_2002_115-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Soon coffee became the primary commodity export of Sri Lanka. Falling coffee prices as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1847" title="Panic of 1847">depression of 1847</a> stalled economic development and prompted the governor to introduce a series of taxes on firearms, dogs, shops, boats, etc., and to reintroduce a form of <i>rajakariya</i>, requiring six days free labour on roads or payment of a cash equivalent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nubin_2002_115_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nubin_2002_115-104">[104]</a></sup> These harsh measures antagonised the locals, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matale_Rebellion" title="Matale Rebellion">another rebellion</a> broke out in 1848.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matale1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-matale1-105">[105]</a></sup> A devastating leaf disease, <i><a href="/wiki/Hemileia_vastatrix" title="Hemileia vastatrix">Hemileia vastatrix</a></i>, struck the coffee plantations in 1869, destroying the entire industry within fifteen years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The British quickly found a replacement: abandoning coffee, they began cultivating tea instead. <a href="/wiki/Tea_production_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Tea production in Sri Lanka">Tea production in Sri Lanka</a> thrived in the following decades. Large-scale rubber plantations began in the early 20th century.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="1006" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG/320px-Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG/480px-Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG/640px-Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kandyan_Chiefs_in_1905.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British appointed Kandyan chiefs, 1905</div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of the 19th century, a new educated <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social class</a> transcending race and <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a> arose through British attempts to staff the <a href="/wiki/Ceylon_Civil_Service" title="Ceylon Civil Service">Ceylon Civil Service</a> and the legal, educational, and medical professions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> New leaders represented the various ethnic groups of the population in the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_Ceylon" title="Legislative Council of Ceylon">Ceylon Legislative Council</a> on a communal basis. Buddhist and Hindu revivalism reacted against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_(Christianity)" title="Mission (Christianity)">Christian missionary</a> activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tamlwk_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-tamlwk-109">[109]</a></sup> The first two decades in the 20th century are noted by the unique harmony among Sinhalese and <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil</a> political leadership, which has since been lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1919, major Sinhalese and Tamil political organisations united to form the Ceylon National Congress, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Ponnambalam_Arunachalam" title="Ponnambalam Arunachalam">Ponnambalam Arunachalam</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> pressing colonial masters for more constitutional reforms. But without massive popular support, and with the governor\'s encouragement for "communal representation" by creating a "Colombo seat" that dangled between Sinhalese and Tamils, the Congress lost momentum towards the mid-1920s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Donoughmore_Constitution" title="Donoughmore Constitution">Donoughmore reforms</a> of 1931 repudiated the communal representation and introduced <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal adult franchise</a> (the franchise stood at 4% before the reforms). This step was strongly criticised by the Tamil political leadership, who realised that they would be reduced to a minority in the newly created <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_Ceylon" title="State Council of Ceylon">State Council of Ceylon</a>, which succeeded the legislative council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tamllib_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-tamllib-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In 1937, Tamil leader <a href="/wiki/G._G._Ponnambalam" title="G. G. Ponnambalam">G. G. Ponnambalam</a> demanded a 50&#8211;50 representation (50% for the Sinhalese and 50% for other ethnic groups) in the State Council. However, this demand was not met by the <a href="/wiki/Soulbury_Commission" title="Soulbury Commission">Soulbury reforms</a> of 1944&#8211;45.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Sri_Lanka">Modern Sri Lanka</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_independence_movement" title="Sri Lankan independence movement">Sri Lankan independence movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sri_Lanka_(1948%E2%80%93present)" title="History of Sri Lanka (1948&#8211;present)">History of Sri Lanka (1948&#8211;present)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Sri Lankan Civil War">Sri Lankan Civil War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SL_Independence.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/SL_Independence.jpg/220px-SL_Independence.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/SL_Independence.jpg/330px-SL_Independence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/SL_Independence.jpg/440px-SL_Independence.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SL_Independence.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The formal ceremony marking the start of self-rule, with the opening of the first parliament at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_Square,_Colombo" title="Independence Square, Colombo">Independence Square</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Soulbury constitution ushered in <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Dominion status</a>, with independence proclaimed on 4 February 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-countrst68_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-countrst68-115">[115]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_Stephen_Senanayake" title="Don Stephen Senanayake">D. S. Senanayake</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Prime Minister of Sri Lanka">Prime Minister of Ceylon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS-116">[116]</a></sup> Prominent <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil</a> leaders including Ponnambalam and <a href="/wiki/Arunachalam_Mahadeva" title="Arunachalam Mahadeva">Arunachalam Mahadeva</a> joined his cabinet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tamllib_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-tamllib-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British Royal Navy</a> remained stationed at <a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a> until 1956. A countrywide popular demonstration against withdrawal of the rice ration, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartal_1953" title="Hartal 1953">Hartal 1953</a>, resulted in the resignation of prime minister <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Senanayake" title="Dudley Senanayake">Dudley Senanayake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islnksd_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-islnksd-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/S._W._R._D._Bandaranaike" title="S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike">S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike</a> was elected prime minister in 1956. His three-year rule had a profound impact through his self-proclaimed role of "defender of the besieged Sinhalese culture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> He introduced the controversial <a href="/wiki/Sinhala_Only_Act" title="Sinhala Only Act">Sinhala Only Act</a>, recognising <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinhala_language" title="Sinhala language">Sinhala</a> as the only official language of the government. Although partially reversed in 1958, the bill posed a grave concern for the Tamil community, which perceived in it a threat to their language and culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FW_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FW-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AV_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-AV-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a1_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-a1-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Illankai_Tamil_Arasu_Kachchi" title="Illankai Tamil Arasu Kachchi">Federal Party</a> (FP) launched a movement of non-violent resistance (<a href="/wiki/Satyagraha" title="Satyagraha">satyagraha</a>) against the bill, which prompted Bandaranaike to reach an agreement (<a href="/wiki/Bandaranaike%E2%80%93Chelvanayakam_Pact" title="Bandaranaike&#8211;Chelvanayakam Pact">Bandaranaike&#8211;Chelvanayakam Pact</a>) with <a href="/wiki/S._J._V._Chelvanayakam" title="S. J. V. Chelvanayakam">S. J. V. Chelvanayakam</a>, leader of the FP, to resolve the looming ethnic conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The pact proved ineffective in the face of ongoing protests by opposition and the Buddhist clergy. The bill, together with various government <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_state-sponsored_colonisation_schemes" title="Sri Lankan state-sponsored colonisation schemes">colonisation schemes</a>, contributed much towards the political rancour between Sinhalese and Tamil political leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Bandaranaike was <a href="/wiki/S._W._R._D._Bandaranaike#Assassination" title="S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike">assassinated</a> by an extremist Buddhist monk in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Sirimavo_Bandaranaike" title="Sirimavo Bandaranaike">Sirimavo Bandaranaike</a>, the widow of Bandaranaike, took office as prime minister in 1960, and withstood an <a href="/wiki/1962_Ceylonese_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1962 Ceylonese coup d\'&#233;tat attempt">attempted coup d\'&#233;tat</a> in 1962. During her second term as prime minister, the government instituted socialist economic policies, strengthening ties with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, while promoting a policy of non-alignment. In 1971, Ceylon experienced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1971_JVP_Insurrection" title="1971 JVP Insurrection">Marxist insurrection</a>, which was quickly suppressed. In 1972, the country became a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> named Sri Lanka, repudiating its dominion status. Prolonged minority grievances and the use of communal emotionalism as an election campaign weapon by both Sinhalese and Tamil leaders abetted a fledgling Tamil militancy in the north during the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Policy_of_standardisation" title="Policy of standardisation">policy of standardisation</a> by the Sirimavo government to rectify disparities created in university enrolment, which was in essence an <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> to assist geographically disadvantaged students to obtain tertiary education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affrmact_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-affrmact-127">[127]</a></sup> resulted in reducing the proportion of Tamil students at university level and acted as the immediate catalyst for the rise of militancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The assassination of <a href="/wiki/Jaffna" title="Jaffna">Jaffna</a> <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">Mayor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_Duraiyappah" title="Alfred Duraiyappah">Alfred Duraiyappah</a> in 1975 by the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam" title="Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam">Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam</a> (LTTE) marked a crisis point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman139_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman139-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rohang_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-rohang-131">[131]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="380" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/66/Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg/220px-Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/66/Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg/330px-Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/66/Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_July_1983_Colombo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Colombo, 1983: The <a href="/wiki/Black_July" title="Black July">Black July</a>, 400&#8211;3000 Tamil civilians were killed across the island in the anti-Tamil Pogrom allegedly backed by hard-line Sinhalese ministers within the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Government of Sri Lanka">government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Remembering_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Remembering-132">[132]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="264" data-file-width="377" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4d/Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg/220px-Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4d/Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg/330px-Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4d/Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Dalada_Maligawa_Attack_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam" title="Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam">Tamil Tigers</a> <a href="/wiki/1998_Temple_of_the_Tooth_attack" title="1998 Temple of the Tooth attack">bombed</a> the sacred <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Dalada_Maligawa" title="Sri Dalada Maligawa">Sri
