Dalada Maligawa</a> temple in 1998.</div></div></div>\n<p>The government of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Junius_Richard_Jayewardene" title="Junius Richard Jayewardene">J. R. Jayawardene</a> swept to power in 1977, defeating the largely unpopular <a href="/wiki/United_Front_(Sri_Lanka)" title="United Front (Sri Lanka)">United Front</a> government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-attms_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-attms-133">[133]</a></sup> Jayawardene introduced a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Constitution of Sri Lanka">new constitution</a>, together with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free-market_economy" title="Free-market economy">free-market economy</a> and a powerful <a href="/wiki/Executive_president" title="Executive president">executive presidency</a> modelled after that of France. It made Sri Lanka the first <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> country to <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalise</a> its economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filbrn_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-filbrn-134">[134]</a></sup> Beginning in 1983, ethnic tensions were manifested in an <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Sri Lankan Civil War">on-and-off insurgency</a> against the government by the LTTE. An LTTE attack on 13 soldiers resulted in the anti-Tamil <a href="/wiki/Black_July" title="Black July">race riots</a> in July 1983, allegedly backed by <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_Buddhist_nationalism" title="Sinhalese Buddhist nationalism">Sinhalese hard-line</a> ministers, which resulted in more than 150,000 Tamil civilians fleeing the island, seeking asylum in other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Remembering_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Remembering-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lkwbblk_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-lkwbblk-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lapses in foreign policy resulted in India strengthening the Tigers by providing arms and training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sndaytst_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-sndaytst-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> In 1987, the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Sri_Lanka_Accord" title="Indo-Sri Lanka Accord">Indo-Sri Lanka Accord</a> was signed and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Peace_Keeping_Force" title="Indian Peace Keeping Force">Indian Peace Keeping Force</a> (IPKF) was deployed in northern Sri Lanka to stabilise the region by neutralising the LTTE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stokke2000a_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stokke2000a-139">[139]</a></sup> The same year, the <a href="/wiki/Janatha_Vimukthi_Peramuna" title="Janatha Vimukthi Peramuna">JVP</a> launched its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9389_JVP_Insurrection" title="1987&#8211;89 JVP Insurrection">second insurrection</a> in Southern Sri Lanka,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secninsr_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-secninsr-140">[140]</a></sup> necessitating redeployment of the IPKF in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atimes_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-atimes-141">[141]</a></sup> In October 1990, the LTTE <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Muslims_from_the_Northern_province_by_LTTE" title="Expulsion of Muslims from the Northern province by LTTE">expelled Sri Lankan Moors</a> (Muslims by religion) from northern Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slnp_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-slnp-142">[142]</a></sup> In 2002, the Sri Lankan government and LTTE signed a Norwegian-mediated ceasefire agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a1_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-a1-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1686" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG/220px-ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG/330px-ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG/440px-ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ColomboHarbour-August2013-01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombo_Harbour" title="Colombo Harbour">Colombo Harbour</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(Colombo)" title="World Trade Center (Colombo)">World Trade Center</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Ceylon" title="Bank of Ceylon">BOC tower</a> in the background</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Asian tsunami</a> killed over 35,000 in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsws1_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsws1-143">[143]</a></sup> From 1985 to 2006, the Sri Lankan government and Tamil insurgents held four rounds of peace talks without success. Both LTTE and the government resumed fighting in 2006, and the government officially backed out of the ceasefire in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a1_122-2"><a href="#cite_note-a1-122">[122]</a></sup> In 2009, under the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sri_Lanka" title="President of Sri Lanka">Presidency</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mahinda_Rajapaksa" title="Mahinda Rajapaksa">Mahinda Rajapaksa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lanka Armed Forces</a> defeated the LTTE and re-established control of the entire country by the Sri Lankan Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Overall, between 60,000 and 100,000 people were killed during the 26 years of conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC200509_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC200509-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Forty thousand Tamil civilians <a href="/wiki/List_of_attacks_on_civilians_attributed_to_Sri_Lankan_government_forces" title="List of attacks on civilians attributed to Sri Lankan government forces">may have been killed</a> in the final phases of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_civil_war" title="Sri Lankan civil war">Sri Lankan civil war</a>, according to an Expert Panel convened by <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>. The exact number of Tamils killed is still a speculation that needs further study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Following the LTTE\'s defeat, the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_National_Alliance" title="Tamil National Alliance">Tamil National Alliance</a>, the largest Tamil political party in Sri Lanka, dropped its demand for a <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Eelam" title="Tamil Eelam">separate state</a> in favour of a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> solution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The final stages of the war left some 294,000 people displaced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obs320_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-obs320-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The UN Human Rights Council has documented over 12,000 named individuals who have undergone disappearance after detention by security forces in Sri Lanka, the second highest figure in the world since the Working Group came into being in 1980. In March 2009, 378 people had been killed in one day and at least another 1,212 injured. The report was based only on those casualties brought to the hospital. The UN described the situation as a "bloodbath", and one that its Colombo office had been warning against for some time. Their spokesperson Gordon Weiss said that over 100 children had been killed over the weekend in the "large-scale killing of civilans",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the Ministry of Resettlement, most of the displaced persons had been released or returned to their places of origin, leaving only 6,651 in the camps as of December 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sitrep1215_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-sitrep1215-153">[153]</a></sup> In May 2010, President Rajapaksa appointed the <a href="/wiki/Lessons_Learnt_and_Reconciliation_Commission" title="Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission">Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation Commission</a> (LLRC) to assess the conflict between the time of the ceasefire agreement in 2002 and the defeat of the LTTE in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS161211_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS161211-155">[155]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has emerged from its 26-year war to become one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">fastest growing economies</a> of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessinsider1_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider1-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meryl_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-meryl-157">[157]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>During Sri Lanka\'s 68th national independence day celebrations on 4 February 2016, the Tamil version of the national anthem "<a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Matha" title="Sri Lanka Matha">Sri Lanka Matha</a>" was sung for the first time since 1949 at an official government event, the independence day celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Lifting of the unofficial ban on the Tamil version had been approved by President <a href="/wiki/Maithripala_Sirisena" title="Maithripala Sirisena">Maithripala Sirisena</a> (who had said he would unite the nation after the nearly 26-year civil war that ended in 2009) and by others in the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> This step was viewed as part of the plan for reconciliation. Other steps are also being taken to mend ethnic divisions between the Sinhalese majority and the Tamil minority, according to a November 2016 article in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)"><i>National Geographic</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> "Sri Lanka Matha" was also sung in the majority Sinhalese. Some groups, and Sri Lanka\'s former President Mahinda Rajapaksa, were opposed to the government officially allowing the Tamil version to be sung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Geography of Sri Lanka">Geography of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg"><img alt="A roughly oval island with a mountainous center" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg/170px-Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg/255px-Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg/340px-Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topography_Sri_Lanka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Sri Lanka</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka lies on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Plate" title="Indian Plate">Indian Plate</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic plate</a> that was formerly part of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Australian_Plate" title="Indo-Australian Plate">Indo-Australian Plate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> It is in the Indian Ocean southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>, between latitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">5&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_north" title="10th parallel north">10&#176;N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/79th_meridian_east" title="79th meridian east">79&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/82nd_meridian_east" title="82nd meridian east">82&#176;E</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Sri Lanka is separated from the mainland portion of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mannar" title="Gulf of Mannar">Gulf of Mannar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palk_Strait" title="Palk Strait">Palk Strait</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam%27s_Bridge" title="Adam\'s Bridge">a land bridge</a> existed between the Indian mainland and Sri Lanka. It now amounts to only a chain of limestone shoals remaining above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Legends claim that it was passable on foot up to 1480 AD, until <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a> deepened the channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garg1992_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Garg1992-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Portions are still as shallow as 1 metre (3&#160;ft), hindering navigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> The island consists mostly of flat to rolling coastal plains, with mountains rising only in the south-central part. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Pidurutalagala" title="Pidurutalagala">Pidurutalagala</a>, reaching 2,524 metres (8,281&#160;ft) above sea level. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Paada1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2012" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sri_Paada1.JPG/220px-Sri_Paada1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sri_Paada1.JPG/330px-Sri_Paada1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sri_Paada1.JPG/440px-Sri_Paada1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Paada1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Adam%27s_Peak" title="Adam\'s Peak">Sripada</a> from <a href="/wiki/Maskeliya" title="Maskeliya">Maskeliya</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka has 103 rivers. The longest of these is the <a href="/wiki/Mahaweli_River" title="Mahaweli River">Mahaweli River</a>, extending 335 kilometres (208&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> These waterways give rise to 51 natural waterfalls of 10 meters or more. The highest is <a href="/wiki/Bambarakanda_Falls" title="Bambarakanda Falls">Bambarakanda Falls</a>, with a height of 263 metres (863&#160;ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Sri Lanka\'s coastline is 1,585&#160;km long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-unep-173">[173]</a></sup> Sri Lanka claims an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> (EEZ) extending 200 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a>, which is approximately 6.7 times Sri Lanka\'s land area. The coastline and adjacent waters support highly productive marine ecosystems such as <a href="/wiki/Fringing_reef" title="Fringing reef">fringing</a> <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and shallow beds of coastal and <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuarine</a> <a href="/wiki/Seagrass" title="Seagrass">seagrasses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faosl_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-faosl-174">[174]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka has 45 <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> and 40 <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-unep-173">[173]</a></sup> Sri Lanka\'s <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> ecosystem spans over 7,000 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> and played a vital role in buffering the force of the waves in the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean tsunami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iucnas_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-iucnas-175">[175]</a></sup> The island is rich in minerals such as <a href="/wiki/Ilmenite" title="Ilmenite">ilmenite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feldspar" title="Feldspar">feldspar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graphite" title="Graphite">graphite</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">silica</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaolin" title="Kaolin">kaolin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mica" title="Mica">mica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-minr_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-minr-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thor_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-thor-177">[177]</a></sup> Existence of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and gas in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mannar" title="Gulf of Mannar">Gulf of Mannar</a> has also been confirmed and the extraction of recoverable quantities is underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prdssl_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-prdssl-178">[178]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sri Lanka map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<p>The climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> and warm, due to the moderating effects of ocean winds. Mean temperatures range from 17&#160;&#176;C (62.6&#160;&#176;F) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Central Highlands (Sri Lanka)">central highlands</a>, where frost may occur for several days in the winter, to a maximum of 33&#160;&#176;C (91.4&#160;&#176;F) in other low-altitude areas. Average yearly temperatures range from 28&#160;&#176;C (82.4&#160;&#176;F) to nearly 31&#160;&#176;C (87.8&#160;&#176;F). Day and night temperatures may vary by 14&#160;&#176;C (25.2&#160;&#176;F) to 18&#160;&#176;C (32.4&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rainfall pattern is influenced by <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> winds from the Indian Ocean and Bay of Bengal. The "wet zone" and some of the windward slopes of the central highlands receive up to 2,500 millimetres (98.4&#160;in) of rain each year, but the leeward slopes in the east and northeast receive little rain. Most of the east, southeast, and northern parts of Sri Lanka comprise the "dry zone", which receives between 1,200 and 1,900&#160;mm (47 and 75&#160;in) of rain annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The arid northwest and southeast coasts receive the least amount of rain at 800 to 1,200&#160;mm (31 to 47&#160;in) per year. Periodic squalls occur and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a> bring overcast skies and rains to the southwest, northeast, and eastern parts of the island. Humidity is typically higher in the southwest and mountainous areas and depends on the seasonal patterns of rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An increase in average rainfall coupled with heavier rainfall events has resulted in recurrent flooding and related damages to infrastructure, utility supply and the urban economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Environment of Sri Lanka">Environment of Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Wildlife of Sri Lanka">Wildlife of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG/220px-Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG/330px-Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG/440px-Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_Elephants.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_elephant" title="Sri Lankan elephant">Sri Lankan elephant</a> is one of three recognised <a href="/wiki/Subspecies" title="Subspecies">subspecies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a>. The 2011 elephant census estimated a population of 5,879.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Lying within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indomalaya_ecozone" title="Indomalaya ecozone">Indomalaya ecozone</a>, Sri Lanka is one of 25 <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspots</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Although the country is relatively small in size, it has the highest <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> density in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> A remarkably high proportion of the species among its flora and fauna, 27% of the 3,210 <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> and 22% of the <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> (<i>see <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Sri_Lanka" title="List of mammals of Sri Lanka">List</a></i>), are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has declared 24 wildlife reserves, which are home to a wide range of native species such as <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sloth_bear" title="Sloth bear">sloth bears</a>, the unique small loris, a variety of deer, the <a href="/wiki/Purple-faced_langur" title="Purple-faced langur">purple-faced langur</a>, the endangered <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porcupine" title="Porcupine">porcupines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_pangolin" title="Indian pangolin">Indian pangolins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Flowering <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacias</a> flourish on the arid <a href="/wiki/Jaffna_Peninsula" title="Jaffna Peninsula">Jaffna Peninsula</a>. Among the trees of the dry-land forests are valuable species such as <a href="/wiki/Chloroxylon" title="Chloroxylon">satinwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebony" title="Ebony">ebony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesua_ferrea" title="Mesua ferrea">ironwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">mahogany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teak" title="Teak">teak</a>. The wet zone is a tropical <a href="/wiki/Evergreen_forest" title="Evergreen forest">evergreen forest</a> with tall trees, broad foliage, and a dense undergrowth of vines and creepers. Subtropical evergreen forests resembling those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">temperate climates</a> flourish in the higher altitudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rainbirder_-_Leopard_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="676" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg/220px-Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg/330px-Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg/440px-Rainbirder_-_Leopard_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rainbirder_-_Leopard_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_leopard" title="Sri Lankan leopard">Sri Lankan leopard</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panthera_pardus_kotiya" title="Panthera pardus kotiya">Panthera pardus kotiya</a></i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a> native to Sri Lanka.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Yala_National_Park" title="Yala National Park">Yala National Park</a> in the southeast protects herds of elephant, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peacock" title="Peacock">peacocks</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Wilpattu_National_Park" title="Wilpattu National Park">Wilpattu National Park</a> in the northwest, the largest national park, preserves the habitats of many water birds such as <a href="/wiki/Stork" title="Stork">storks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelican" title="Pelican">pelicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibis" title="Ibis">ibis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spoonbill" title="Spoonbill">spoonbills</a>. The island has four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" title="Biosphere reserve">biosphere reserves</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bundala_National_Park" title="Bundala National Park">Bundala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurulu_Forest_Reserve" title="Hurulu Forest Reserve">Hurulu Forest Reserve</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kanneliya-Dediyagala-Nakiyadeniya" title="Kanneliya-Dediyagala-Nakiyadeniya">Kanneliya-Dediyagala-Nakiyadeniya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sinharaja_Forest_Reserve" title="Sinharaja Forest Reserve">Sinharaja</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_biosphere_reserves_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco_biosphere_reserves-189">[189]</a></sup> Of these, Sinharaja forest reserve is home to 26 endemic birds and 20 rainforest species, including the elusive <a href="/wiki/Red-faced_malkoha" title="Red-faced malkoha">red-faced malkoha</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Green-billed_coucal" title="Green-billed coucal">green-billed coucal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_blue_magpie" title="Sri Lanka blue magpie">Sri Lanka blue magpie</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1356" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg/220px-Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg/330px-Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg/440px-Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhododendron_arboreum_zeylanicum_flower.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maha rath mala (<i>Rhododendron arboreum</i> ssp. <i>zeylanicum</i>) is a rare sub-species of <i><a href="/wiki/Rhododendron_arboreum" title="Rhododendron arboreum">Rhododendron arboreum</a></i> found in <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Central Highlands of Sri Lanka">Central Highlands of Sri Lanka</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The untapped genetic potential of Sinharaja flora is enormous. Of the 211 woody trees and lianas within the reserve, 139 (66%) are endemic. The total vegetation density, including trees, shrubs, herbs and seedlings, has been estimated at 240,000 individuals per <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectare</a>. The Minneriya National Park borders the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneriya_tank" title="Minneriya tank">Minneriya tank</a>, which is an important source of water for numerous elephants (Elephus maximus) inhabiting the surrounding forests. Dubbed "The Gathering", the congregation of elephants can be seen on the tank-bed in the late dry season (August to October) as the surrounding water sources steadily disappear. The park also encompasses a range of micro-habitats which include classic dry zone tropical monsoonal evergreen forest, thick stands of giant bamboo, hilly pastures (patanas). and grasslands (talawas).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minneriya_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minneriya-190">[190]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka is home to over 250 types of resident birds (<i>see <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Sri_Lanka" title="List of birds of Sri Lanka">List</a></i>). It has declared several bird sanctuaries including Kumana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kumnas_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-kumnas-191">[191]</a></sup> During the Mahaweli Program of the 1970s and 1980s in northern Sri Lanka, the government set aside four areas of land totalling 1,900&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (730&#160;sq&#160;mi) as national parks. Sri Lanka\'s forest cover, which was around 49% in 1920, had fallen to approximately 24% by 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coverf_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-coverf-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-193">[193]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Politics of Sri Lanka">Politics of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Parliament_Building,_Colombo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3310" data-file-width="4965" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG/220px-Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG/330px-Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG/440px-Old_Parliament_Building%2C_Colombo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Parliament_Building,_Colombo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_Parliament_Building,_Colombo" title="Old Parliament Building, Colombo">old Sri Lankan parliament building</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Galle_Face_Green" title="Galle Face Green">Galle Face Green</a>. It now serves as the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Secretariat" title="Presidential Secretariat">Presidential Secretariat</a>\'s headquarters.</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Donoughmore_Constitution" title="Donoughmore Constitution">Donoughmore Constitution</a>, drafted by the <a href="/wiki/Donoughmore_Commission" title="Donoughmore Commission">Donoughmore Commission</a> in 1931, enabled <a href="/wiki/General_election" title="General election">general elections</a> with adult <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> (universal adult voting) in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-janerus_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-janerus-195">[195]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylonese_State_Council_election,_1931" title="Ceylonese State Council election, 1931">first election</a> under the universal adult franchise, held in June 1931, was for the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_Ceylon" title="State Council of Ceylon">Ceylon State Council</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/Don_Baron_Jayatilaka" title="Don Baron Jayatilaka">Don Baron Jayatilaka</a> was elected as Leader of the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1944, the <a href="/wiki/Soulbury_Commission" title="Soulbury Commission">Soulbury Commission</a> was appointed to draft a new constitution. During this time, struggle for independence was fought on "constitutionalist" lines under the leadership of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_Stephen_Senanayake" title="Don Stephen Senanayake">D. S. Senanayake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The draft constitution was enacted in the same year, and Senanayake was appointed Prime Minister following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylonese_parliamentary_election,_1947" title="Ceylonese parliamentary election, 1947">parliamentary election in 1947</a>. The Soulbury constitution ushered in <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a> status and granted independence to Sri Lanka in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-janerus_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-janerus-195">[195]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span></h3>\n<p>The current political culture in Sri Lanka is a contest between two rival coalitions led by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre-left" title="Centre-left">centre-leftist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progressivist" title="Progressivist">progressivist</a> <a href="/wiki/United_People%27s_Freedom_Alliance" title="United People\'s Freedom Alliance">United People\'s Freedom Alliance</a> (UPFA), an offspring of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Freedom_Party" title="Sri Lanka Freedom Party">Sri Lanka Freedom Party</a> (SLFP), and the comparatively <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wing</a> and pro-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitalist" title="Capitalist">capitalist</a> <a href="/wiki/United_National_Party" title="United National Party">United National Party</a> (UNP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Sri Lanka is essentially a multi-party democracy with many smaller Buddhist, socialist and Tamil nationalist political parties. As of July 2011, the number of registered political parties in the country is 67.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Of these, the <a href="/wiki/Lanka_Sama_Samaja_Party" title="Lanka Sama Samaja Party">Lanka Sama Samaja Party</a> (LSSP), established in 1935, is the oldest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The UNP, established by D. S. Senanayake in 1946, was until recently the largest single political party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpl_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-unpl-201">[201]</a></sup> It is the only political group which had representation in all parliaments since independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpl_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-unpl-201">[201]</a></sup> SLFP was founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solomon_West_Ridgeway_Dias_Bandaranaike" title="Solomon West Ridgeway Dias Bandaranaike">S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike</a>, who was the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">Cabinet minister</a> of Local Administration before he left the UNP in July 1951.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slfps_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-slfps-202">[202]</a></sup> SLFP registered its first victory in 1956, defeating the ruling UNP in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylonese_parliamentary_election,_1956" title="Ceylonese parliamentary election, 1956">1956 Parliamentary election</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slfps_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-slfps-202">[202]</a></sup> Following the parliamentary election in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylonese_parliamentary_election,_July_1960" title="Ceylonese parliamentary election, July 1960">July 1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sirimavo_Bandaranaike" title="Sirimavo Bandaranaike">Sirimavo Bandaranaike</a> became the prime minister and the world\'s first elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_elected_or_appointed_female_heads_of_government" title="List of elected or appointed female heads of government">female head of government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcsirimavo_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsirimavo-203">[203]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/G._G._Ponnambalam" title="G. G. Ponnambalam">G. G. Ponnambalam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamil_nationalism" title="Sri Lankan Tamil nationalism">Tamil nationalist</a> counterpart of S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-socs_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-socs-204">[204]</a></sup> founded the <a href="/wiki/All_Ceylon_Tamil_Congress" title="All Ceylon Tamil Congress">All Ceylon Tamil Congress</a> (ACTC) in 1944. Objecting to Ponnambalam\'s cooperation with D. S. Senanayake, a dissident group led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S.J.V._Chelvanayakam" title="S.J.V. Chelvanayakam">S.J.V. Chelvanayakam</a> broke away in 1949 and formed the <a href="/wiki/Illankai_Tamil_Arasu_Kachchi" title="Illankai Tamil Arasu Kachchi">Illankai Tamil Arasu Kachchi</a> (ITAK), also known as the Federal Party, becoming the main Tamil political party in Sri Lanka for next two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poltitak_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-poltitak-205">[205]</a></sup> The Federal Party advocated a more aggressive stance toward the Sinhalese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postcolhist_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-postcolhist-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the constitutional reforms of 1972, the All Ceylon Tamil Congress (ACTC) and Illankai Tamil Arasu Kachchi (ITAK) created a common front called the Tamil United Front (later <a href="/wiki/Tamil_United_Liberation_Front" title="Tamil United Liberation Front">Tamil United Liberation Front</a>). Following a period of turbulence as Tamil militants rose to power in the late 1970s, these Tamil political parties were succeeded in October 2001 by the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_National_Alliance" title="Tamil National Alliance">Tamil National Alliance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postcolhist_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-postcolhist-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tnas_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-tnas-207">[207]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Janatha_Vimukthi_Peramuna" title="Janatha Vimukthi Peramuna">Janatha Vimukthi Peramuna</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" title="Marxist&#8211;Leninist">Marxist&#8211;Leninist</a> political party founded by <a href="/wiki/Rohana_Wijeweera" title="Rohana Wijeweera">Rohana Wijeweera</a> in 1965, serves as a third force in the current political context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jvpnew_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-jvpnew-208">[208]</a></sup> It endorses leftist policies which are more radical than the traditionalist leftist politics of the LSSP and the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Communist Party of Sri Lanka">Communist Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postcolhist_206-2"><a href="#cite_note-postcolhist-206">[206]</a></sup> Founded in 1981, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Muslim_Congress" title="Sri Lanka Muslim Congress">Sri Lanka Muslim Congress</a> is the largest Muslim political party in Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muslcon_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-muslcon-209">[209]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Constitution of Sri Lanka">Constitution of Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Elections in Sri Lanka">Elections in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background:#EEEEEE; font-size: 100%; white-space: water lily</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Tree</th><td><a href="/wiki/Mesua_ferrea" title="Mesua ferrea">Ceylon ironwood</a> (n&#257;)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Sport</th><td><a hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Sri_Lankan_symbols" title="Template:Sri Lankan symbols"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg/220px-Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg/330px-Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg/440px-Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_Colombo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Supreme Court of Sri Lanka, Colombo</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka is a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> which is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a>, with a mixture of a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constnt_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-constnt-212">[212]</a></sup> Most provisions of the constitution can be amended by a <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">two-thirds majority</a> in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Parliament of Sri Lanka">parliament</a>. The amendment of <a href="/wiki/Entrenched_clause" title="Entrenched clause">certain basic features</a> such as the clauses on language, religion, and reference to Sri Lanka as a unitary state require both a two-thirds majority and approval in a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>.\n</p><p>In common with many democracies, the Sri Lankan government has three branches:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive</a></b>: The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sri_Lanka" title="President of Sri Lanka">President of Sri Lanka</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_in_chief" title="Commander in chief">commander in chief</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Military of Sri Lanka">armed forces</a>; <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and is popularly elected for a five-year term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The President heads the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a> and appoints <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">ministers</a> from elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">members of parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> The president is immune from legal proceedings while in office with respect to any acts done or omitted to be done by him or her in either an official or private capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Following passage of the <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_Constitution_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Nineteenth Amendment to the Constitution of Sri Lanka">19th amendment to the constitution</a> in 2015, the President has two terms, which previously stood at no term limit.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative</a></b>: The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Parliament of Sri Lanka">Parliament of Sri Lanka</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> 225-member <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a> with 196 members elected in multi-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constituency" title="Constituency">constituencies</a> and 29 elected by <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Members are elected by universal suffrage for a five-year term. The president may summon, suspend, or end a legislative session and dissolve Parliament any time after four and a half years. The parliament reserves the power to make all laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliam_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-parliam-217">[217]</a></sup> The president\'s deputy, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_minister_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Prime minister of Sri Lanka">Prime Minister</a>, leads the <a href="/wiki/Ruling_party" title="Ruling party">ruling party</a> in parliament and shares many executive responsibilities, mainly in domestic affairs.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judicial</a></b>: Sri Lanka\'s judiciary consists of a <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Supreme Court of Sri Lanka">Supreme Court</a> &#8211; the highest and final superior court of record,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliam_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-parliam-217">[217]</a></sup> a Court of Appeal, High Courts and a number of subordinate courts. The highly complex legal system reflects diverse cultural influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpanh_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-unpanh-218">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law" title="Criminal law">Criminal law</a> is based almost entirely on <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">British law</a>. Basic <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">Civil law</a> derives from <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Netherlands" title="Law of the Netherlands">Dutch law</a>. Laws pertaining to marriage, divorce, and inheritance are <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">communal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lawsd_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-lawsd-219">[219]</a></sup> Due to ancient customary practices and/or religion, the Sinhala customary law (Kandyan law), the <a href="/wiki/Thesavalamai" title="Thesavalamai">Thesavalamai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia law</a> are followed in special cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-custmryl_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-custmryl-220">[220]</a></sup> The President appoints judges to the Supreme Court, the Court of Appeal, and the High Courts. A judicial service commission, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Chief Justice of Sri Lanka">Chief Justice</a> and two Supreme Court judges, appoints, transfers, and dismisses lower court judges.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div class="floatright noresize" role="img" style="width: //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_the_Southern_Province_%28Sri_Lanka%29.PNG/50px-Flag_of_the_Southern_Province_%28Sri_Lanka%29.PNG 2x" width="25"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Administrative divisions of Sri Lanka">Administrative divisions of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>For administrative purposes, Sri Lanka is divided into nine <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Provinces of Sri Lanka">provinces</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> and twenty-five <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Districts of Sri Lanka">districts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Provinces</b>\nThere have been provinces in Sri Lanka since the 19th century, but they had no legal status until 1987 when the 13th Amendment to the 1978 constitution established provincial councils after several decades of increasing demand for a <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">decentralisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Government of Sri Lanka">Government of Sri Lanka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-official-223">[223]</a></sup> Each provincial council is an autonomous body not under the authority of any Ministry. Some of its functions had been undertaken by central government ministries, departments, corporations, and statutory authorities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-official-223">[223]</a></sup> but authority over land and police is not as a rule given to provincial councils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landpolc_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-landpolc-224">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landpolc2_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-landpolc2-225">[225]</a></sup> Between 1989 and 2006, the Northern and Eastern provinces were temporarily merged to form the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Province_(Sri_Lanka)" title="North Eastern Province (Sri Lanka)">North-East Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lnpx_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-lnpx-226">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norteastn_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-norteastn-227">[227]</a></sup> Prior to 1987, all administrative tasks for the provinces were handled by a <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Districts of Sri Lanka">district-based</a> civil service which had been in place since <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">colonial times</a>. Now each province is administered by a directly elected provincial council:\n</p>\n<table border="0" class="toc" style="width:50%; font-size:90%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="8" style="background:#629BAB; text-align:right">4,902\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">1,893\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right"><center>1,919,478</center>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Southern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Southern Province, Sri Lanka">Southern</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5,559\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2,146\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><center>2,465,626</center>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0"><a href="/wiki/Uva_Province" title="Uva Province">Uva</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0"><a href="/wiki/Badulla" title="Badulla">Badulla</a>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">8,488\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">3,277\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right"><center>1,259,419</center>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Western_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Western Province, Sri Lanka">Western</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3,709\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,432\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><center>5,837,294</center>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Districts and local authorities</b>\nSri Lanka is also divided into 25 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Districts of Sri Lanka">districts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-distrsl_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-distrsl-228">[228]</a></sup> Each district is administered under a <a href="/wiki/Government_Agent_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Government Agent (Sri Lanka)">District Secretariat</a>. The districts are further subdivided into 256 <a href="/wiki/Divisional_Secretariats_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Divisional Secretariats of Sri Lanka">divisional secretariats</a>, and these, in turn, to approximately 14,008 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grama_Niladharis_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Grama Niladharis of Sri Lanka">Grama Niladhari</a> divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tstasgov_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-tstasgov-229">[229]</a></sup> The Districts are known in Sinhala as <i>Disa</i> and in Tamil as <i>M&#257;waddam</i>. Originally, a Disa (usually rendered into English as Dissavony) was a <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">duchy</a>, notably Matale and Uva. A <a href="/wiki/Government_Agent_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Government Agent (Sri Lanka)">government agent</a>, who is known as <i>District Secretary</i>, administers a district.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg/220px-Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg/330px-Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg/440px-Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_lanka_southern_province_aerial_view.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aerial view of Southern Province.</div></div></div>\n<p>There are three other types of local authorities: Municipal Councils (18), Urban councils (13) and Pradeshiya Sabha, also called Pradesha Sabhai (256).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Local authorities were originally based on feudal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counties" title="Counties">counties</a> named <i>korale</i> and <i>rata</i>, and were formerly known as \'D.R.O. divisions\' after the \'Divisional Revenue Officer\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Later the D.R.O.s became \'Assistant Government Agents\' and the divisions were known as \'A.G.A. divisions\'. These Divisional Secretariats are currently administered by a \'Divisional Secretary\'.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Foreign relations of Sri Lanka">Foreign relations of Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lanka Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg/220px-Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg/330px-Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg/440px-Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jayewardene_presents_elephant_to_Reagan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/J._R._Jayewardene" title="J. R. Jayewardene">J. R. Jayewardene</a> gifting a baby elephant to US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> in 1984</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (NAM). While ensuring that it maintains its independence, Sri Lanka has cultivated <a href="/wiki/India%E2%80%93Sri_Lanka_relations" title="India&#8211;Sri Lanka relations">relations with India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-relatns_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-relatns-232">[232]</a></sup> Sri Lanka became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1955. Today, it is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">SAARC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Colombo_Plan" title="Colombo Plan">Colombo Plan</a>.\n</p><p>One of the two parties that have governed Sri Lanka since its independence, the <a href="/wiki/United_National_Party" title="United National Party">United National Party</a>, has traditionally favoured links with the West, while its left-leaning counterpart, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Freedom_Party" title="Sri Lanka Freedom Party">Sri Lanka Freedom Party</a>, has favoured links with the East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-relatns_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-relatns-232">[232]</a></sup> Sri Lankan Finance Minister J. R. Jayewardene, together with then Australian Foreign Minister Sir Percy Spencer, proposed the <a href="/wiki/Colombo_Plan" title="Colombo Plan">Colombo Plan</a> at the Commonwealth Foreign Minister\'s Conference held in Colombo in 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">San Francisco Peace Conference</a> in 1951, while many countries were reluctant, Sri Lanka argued for a free <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and refused to accept payment of reparations for <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> damage because it believed it would harm Japan\'s economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> Sri Lanka-China relations started as soon as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">PRC</a> was formed in 1949. The two countries signed an important Rice-Rubber Pact in 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Sri Lanka played a vital role at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian%E2%80%93African_Conference" title="Asian&#8211;African Conference">Asian&#8211;African Conference</a> in 1955, which was an important step in the crystallisation of the NAM.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Bandaranaike government of 1956 significantly changed the pro-western policies set by the previous UNP government. It recognised <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> under <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> in 1959. Shortly afterward, Cuba\'s revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Ernesto Che Guevara</a> paid a visit to Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirima-Shastri_Pact" title="Sirima-Shastri Pact">Sirima-Shastri Pact</a></i> of 1964<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirima-Gandhi_Pact" title="Sirima-Gandhi Pact">Sirima-Gandhi Pact</a></i> of 1974<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> were signed between Sri Lankan and Indian leaders in an attempt to solve the <a href="/wiki/Ceylon_Citizenship_Act" title="Ceylon Citizenship Act">long-standing dispute</a> over the status of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Tamils_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Indian Tamils of Sri Lanka">plantation workers of Indian origin</a>. In 1974, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kachchatheevu" title="Kachchatheevu">Kachchatheevu</a>, a small island in <a href="/wiki/Palk_Strait" title="Palk Strait">Palk Strait</a>, was formally ceded to Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> By this time, Sri Lanka was strongly involved in the NAM and <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a> held the fifth NAM summit in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> The relationship between Sri Lanka and India became tense under the government of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Junius_Richard_Jayewardene" title="Junius Richard Jayewardene">J. R. Jayawardene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atimes_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-atimes-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indnrel_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-indnrel-242">[242]</a></sup> As a result, <a href="/wiki/Indian_intervention_in_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Indian intervention in the Sri Lankan Civil War">India intervened in the Sri Lankan Civil War</a> and subsequently deployed an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Peace_Keeping_Force" title="Indian Peace Keeping Force">Indian Peace Keeping Force</a> in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> In the present, Sri Lanka enjoys extensive relations with China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px #ddd solid;">\n<caption><b>Branches of the Sri Lanka Armed Forces</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="width:120px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg"><img alt="Sri Lanka Military 0208.jpg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg/160px-Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg/240px-Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg/320px-Sri_Lanka_Military_0208.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Army" title="Sri Lanka Army">Sri Lanka Army</a><br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-55#T-55A" title="T-55">T-55AM2</a> <a href="/wiki/Main_battle_tank" title="Main battle tank">main battle tank</a></small>\n</td>\n<td style="width:120px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SLNS_Sayurala(P623).jpg"><img alt="SLNS Sayurala(P623).jpg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async"
