//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/SLNS_Sayurala%28P623%29.jpg/320px-SLNS_Sayurala%28P623%29.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Navy" title="Sri Lanka Navy">Sri Lanka Navy</a><br/>Flag Ship <a href="/wiki/SLNS_Sayurala_(2016)" title="SLNS Sayurala (2016)">SLNS Sayurala</a></small>\n</td>\n<td style="width:120px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mi24-March2011-01.JPG"><img alt="Mi24-March2011-01.JPG" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="2463" data-file-width="3284" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mi24-March2011-01.JPG/160px-Mi24-March2011-01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mi24-March2011-01.JPG/240px-Mi24-March2011-01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Mi24-March2011-01.JPG/320px-Mi24-March2011-01.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Air_Force" title="Sri Lanka Air Force">Sri Lanka Air Force</a><br/><a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">Mil Mi-24</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attack_Helicopter" title="Attack Helicopter">Attack Helicopter</a></small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Armed_Forces" title="Sri Lanka Armed Forces">Sri Lanka Armed Forces</a>, comprising the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Army" title="Sri Lanka Army">Sri Lanka Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Navy" title="Sri Lanka Navy">Sri Lanka Navy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Air_Force" title="Sri Lanka Air Force">Sri Lanka Air Force</a>, come under the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/purview" title="wikt:purview">purview</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Ministry of Defence (Sri Lanka)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MoD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-247">[247]</a></sup> The total strength of the three services is around 259,000 personnel, with nearly 36,000 reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has not enforced <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">military conscription</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> Paramilitary units include the <a href="/wiki/Special_Task_Force" title="Special Task Force">Special Task Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Civil_Security_Force" title="Sri Lanka Civil Security Force">Civil Security Force</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Coast_Guard" title="Sri Lanka Coast Guard">Sri Lanka Coast Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since independence in 1948, the primary focus of the armed forces has been internal security, crushing three major insurgencies, two by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> militants of the <a href="/wiki/Janatha_Vimukthi_Peramuna" title="Janatha Vimukthi Peramuna">JVP</a> and a 30-year-long conflict with the LTTE which has been <a href="/wiki/Proscription" title="Proscription">proscribed</a> as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrorist_organisation" title="Terrorist organisation">terrorist organisation</a> by <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam#Proscription_as_a_terrorist_group" title="Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam">32 countries</a>. The armed forces have been in a continuous mobilised state for the last 30 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> Marking a rare occurrence in modern military history, the Sri Lankan military was able to bring a decisive end to the Sri Lankan Civil War in May 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has claimed to be the first country in the modern world to eradicate <a href="/wiki/Definitions_of_terrorism" title="Definitions of terrorism">terrorism</a> on its own soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan Armed Forces have engaged in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> operations since the early 1960s, contributing forces to permanent contingents deployed in several UN peacekeeping missions in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_the_Central_African_Republic_and_Chad" title="United Nations Mission in the Central African Republic and Chad">Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilization_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti">Haiti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmissions09_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-unmissions09-256">[256]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Economy of Sri Lanka">Economy of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Agriculture in Sri Lanka">Agriculture in Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea_production_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Tea production in Sri Lanka">Tea production in Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Tourism in Sri Lanka">Tourism in Sri Lanka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Transport in Sri Lanka">Transport in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png/350px-2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png/525px-2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png/700px-2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Sri_Lanka_Products_Export_Treemap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sri Lanka exports by product (2014) from <a class="external text" href="http://atlas.cid.harvard.edu/explore/tree_map/export/lka/all/show/2014/" rel="nofollow">Harvard Atlas of Economic Complexity</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to the International Monetary Fund, Sri Lanka\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> is second only to the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> in the South Asian region in terms of <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2074" data-file-width="3687" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG/220px-OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG/330px-OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG/440px-OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OldParliament-November2015-01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(Colombo)" title="World Trade Center (Colombo)">Colombo World Trade Center</a> in Colombo. <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Secretariat" title="Presidential Secretariat">Presidential Secretariat</a>, Bank of Ceylon and Galadhari Hotel are also visible in the image.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 19th and 20th centuries, Sri Lanka became a <a href="/wiki/Plantation_economy" title="Plantation economy">plantation economy</a> famous for its production and export of <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber">rubber</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon_tea" title="Ceylon tea">Ceylon tea</a>, which remains a trademark national export.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plnyn_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-plnyn-257">[257]</a></sup> The development of modern <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Ports_and_Aviation_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Ministry of Ports and Aviation (Sri Lanka)">ports</a> under British rule raised the strategic importance of the island as a centre of trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-startim_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-startim-258">[258]</a></sup> From 1948 to 1977, <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> strongly influenced the government\'s economic policies. Colonial plantations were dismantled, industries were nationalised, and a <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> established. In 1977, the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market economy</a> was introduced to the country incorporating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulation</a>, and the promotion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_enterprise" title="Private enterprise">private enterprise</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filbrn_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-filbrn-134">[134]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the production and export of tea, rubber, coffee, sugar, and other commodities remain important, industrialisation has increased the importance of <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Textiles" title="Textiles">textiles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>. The country\'s main economic sectors are <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea_production_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Tea production in Sri Lanka">tea export</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">clothing</a>, rice production, and other agricultural products. In addition to these economic sectors, overseas employment, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, contributes substantially in foreign exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lanka&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the service sector makes up 60% of GDP, the industrial sector 28%, and the agriculture sector 12%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> The private sector accounts for 85% of the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adbrep_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-adbrep-260">[260]</a></sup> India is Sri Lanka\'s largest trading partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ionflof_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-ionflof-261">[261]</a></sup> Economic disparities exist between the provinces with the <a href="/wiki/Western_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Western Province, Sri Lanka">Western Province</a> contributing 45.1% of the GDP and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Southern Province, Sri Lanka">Southern Province</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Central Province, Sri Lanka">Central Province</a> contributing 10.7% and 10%, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecdisp_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecdisp-262">[262]</a></sup> With the end of the war, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Sri_Lanka" title="Northern Province, Sri Lanka">Northern Province</a> reported a record 22.9% GDP growth in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-northpr_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-northpr-263">[263]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_030.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1723" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sri_Lanka_030.jpg/220px-Sri_Lanka_030.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sri_Lanka_030.jpg/330px-Sri_Lanka_030.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Sri_Lanka_030.jpg/440px-Sri_Lanka_030.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_030.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sri Lanka\'s most widely known export, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon_tea" title="Ceylon tea">Ceylon tea</a>, which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISO" title="ISO">ISO</a> considers the cleanest tea in the world in terms of pesticide residues. Sri Lanka is also the world\'s 2nd largest exporter of tea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clnst_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-clnst-264">[264]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The per capita income of Sri Lanka has doubled since 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toplsl_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-toplsl-265">[265]</a></sup> During the same period, poverty has dropped from 15.2% to 7.6%, unemployment rate has dropped from 7.2% to 4.9%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Market_capitalisation" title="Market capitalisation">market capitalisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Colombo_Stock_Exchange" title="Colombo Stock Exchange">Colombo Stock Exchange</a> has quadrupled and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" title="Government budget deficit">budget deficit</a> has doubled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-2"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> Over 90% of the households in Sri Lanka are electrified. 87.3% of the population have access to safe drinking water and 39% have access to pipe-borne water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-3"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> Income inequality has also dropped in recent years, indicated by a <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> of 0.36 in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statgovineq_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-statgovineq-266">[266]</a></sup> Sri Lanka\'s cellular subscriber base has shown a staggering 550% growth from 2005 to 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-4"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> Sri Lanka was the first country in the South Asian region to introduce <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a>, 3.5G (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-Speed_Downlink_Packet_Access" title="High-Speed Downlink Packet Access">HSDPA</a>), 3.75G (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-Speed_Uplink_Packet_Access" title="High-Speed Uplink Packet Access">HSUPA</a>) and 4G (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3GPP_Long_Term_Evolution" title="3GPP Long Term Evolution">LTE</a>) mobile telecommunication technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voindnt_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-voindnt-267">[267]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a>, published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, has described Sri Lanka\'s economy as transitioning from the factor-driven stage to the efficiency-driven stage and that it ranks 52nd in global competitiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> Also, out of the 142 countries surveyed, Sri Lanka ranked 45th in health and primary education, 32nd in business sophistication, 42nd in innovation, and 41st in goods market efficiency. Sri Lanka ranks 8th in the <a href="/wiki/World_Giving_Index" title="World Giving Index">World Giving Index</a>, registering high levels of contentment and charitable behaviour in its society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wgix_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-wgix-269">[269]</a></sup> In 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> placed Sri Lanka at the top of its list of 31 places to visit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/S%26P_Dow_Jones_Indices" title="S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices">S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices</a> classifies Sri Lanka as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frontier_market" title="Frontier market">frontier market</a> as of 2018,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> classified it as a <a href="/wiki/3G_(countries)" title="3G (countries)">3G country</a> in February 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Sri Lanka ranks</a> well above other South Asian countries in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) with an index of 0.750.\n</p><p>Sri Lanka\'s road network consists of 35 <a href="/wiki/List_of_A-Grade_highways_in_Sri_Lanka" title="List of A-Grade highways in Sri Lanka">A-Grade highways</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">controlled-access highways</a> (<a href="/wiki/E01_expressway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="E01 expressway (Sri Lanka)">E01</a> and <a href="/wiki/E03_expressway_(Sri_Lanka)" title="E03 expressway (Sri Lanka)">E03</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Rail transport in Sri Lanka">railway network</a>, operated by the state-run <a href="/wiki/National_Railway" title="National Railway">national railway</a> operator <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Railways" title="Sri Lanka Railways">Sri Lanka Railways</a>, spans 1,447 kilometres (900&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Sri Lanka also has three deep-water ports at <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Colombo" title="Port of Colombo">Colombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a>, in addition to the newest port being built at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruhunu_Magampura_International_Port" title="Ruhunu Magampura International Port">Hambantota</a>. The port at Trincomalee is the fifth largest natural harbour in the world; during World War II, the British stated that they could place their entire navy in the harbour with room to spare.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Sri Lanka\'s <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> is <a href="/wiki/SriLankan_Airlines" title="SriLankan Airlines">SriLankan Airlines</a>. Fitch Ratings has affirmed Sri Lanka\'s Foreign- and Local-Currency Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) at \'BB-\' with a "stable" outlook. With a grant of 20 million dollars from the US and help from China, a space academy has been set up for the purpose of developing an indigenous space sector to launch satellites of other nations as well as of Sri Lanka. This dual use of launching technology will also serve to develop missile technology. On 26 September 2012 China launched Sri Lanka\'s first satellite, with plans for more launches in the coming years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the past few years, the country\'s debt has soared as it was developing its infrastructure to the point of near bankruptcy which required a bailout from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> The IMF had agreed to provide a US$1.5 billion bailout loan in April 2016 after Sri Lanka provided a set of criteria intended to improve its economy. By the fourth quarter of 2016, the debt was estimated to be $64.9 billion. Additional debt had been incurred in the past by state-owned organizations and this was said to be at least $9.5 billion. Since early 2015, domestic debt increased by 12 percent and external debt by 25 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2016, the International Monetary Fund reported that the initial disbursement was larger than US$150 million originally planned, a full US$162.6 million (SDR 119.894 million), to Sri Lanka. The agency\'s evaluation for the first tranche  was cautiously optimistic about the future. Under the program Sri Lankan government implemented a new Inland Revenue Act and an automatic fuel pricing formula which were noted by the IMF in its fourth review. In 2018 China agreed to bail out Sri Lanka with a loan of $1.25 billion to deal with  foreign debt repayment spikes in 2019 to 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Demographics of Sri Lanka">Demographics of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SL_population_growth.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="781" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SL_population_growth.png/250px-SL_population_growth.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SL_population_growth.png/375px-SL_population_growth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SL_population_growth.png/500px-SL_population_growth.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SL_population_growth.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sri Lanka\'s population, (1871&#8211;2001)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Sri_Lanka_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka is the 57th most populated nation in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimate_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-estimate-3">[3]</a></sup> with roughly 21,670,000 people, and an annual population growth rate of 1.14%. Sri Lanka has a <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> of 17.6 births per 1,000&#160;people and a <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">death rate</a> of 6.2 deaths per 1,000&#160;people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-5"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> Population density is highest in western Sri Lanka, especially in and around the capital. <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_people" title="Sinhalese people">Sinhalese</a> constitute the largest ethnic group in the country, with 74.8% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPH2011_1_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPH2011_1-284">[284]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamils" title="Sri Lankan Tamils">Sri Lankan Tamils</a> are the second major ethnic group in the island, with a percentage of 11.2%. <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Moors" title="Sri Lankan Moors">Sri Lankan Moors</a> comprise 9.2%. <a href="/wiki/Indian_Tamils_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Indian Tamils of Sri Lanka">Tamils of Indian origin</a> were brought into the country as indentured labourers by British colonists to work on estate plantations. Nearly 50% of them were <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriated</a> following independence in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> They are distinguished from the native Tamil population that has resided in Sri Lanka since ancient times. There are also small ethnic groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burghers</a> (of mixed European descent) and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Malays" title="Sri Lankan Malays">Malays</a> from Southeast Asia. Moreover, there is a small population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedda_people" title="Vedda people">Vedda people</a> who are believed to be the original indigenous group to inhabit the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Languages of Sri Lanka">Languages of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="377" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg/220px-Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg/330px-Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg/440px-Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_Languages_and_Religious_groups_of_Sri_Lanka_1981.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The distribution of languages and religious groups in Sri Lanka,  1981</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" title="Sinhalese language">Sinhalese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> are the two <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a> of Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> The Constitution defines <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as the link language. English is widely used for education, scientific and commercial purposes. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burgher</a> community speak variant forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Creole" title="Portuguese Creole">Portuguese Creole</a> and Dutch with varying proficiency, while members of the Malay community speak a form of <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">Creole</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Malay" title="Sri Lanka Malay">Malay</a> that is unique to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Religion in Sri Lanka">Religion in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Sri Lanka religiosity (<a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew-289">[289]</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:dodgerblue; width:7%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Freedom of religion in Sri Lanka">Other</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:gray; width:0.04%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.04%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="5" style="padding:5px; text-align:left;">Source: Census of Population and Housing, 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPH2011_2_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPH2011_2-290">[290]</a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Sri Lanka is a multi-religious country. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> comprise 70 percent of the population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> school being predominant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bisl-sn_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-bisl-sn-292">[292]</a></sup> Most Buddhists are of the Sinhalese ethnic group. Buddhism was introduced to Sri Lanka in the 2nd century BCE by Venerable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahinda_(buddhist_monk)" title="Mahinda (buddhist monk)">Mahinda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bisl-sn_292-1"><a href="#cite_note-bisl-sn-292">[292]</a></sup> A sapling of the <a href="/wiki/Bodhi_Tree" title="Bodhi Tree">Bodhi Tree</a> under which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Buddha" title="The Buddha">the Buddha</a> attained enlightenment was brought to Sri Lanka during the same time. The <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="P&#257;li Canon">P&#257;li Canon</a> (<i>Thripitakaya</i>), having previously been preserved as an oral tradition, was first committed to writing in Sri Lanka around 30 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ph-tbas_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-ph-tbas-293">[293]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka has the longest continuous history of Buddhism of any predominantly Buddhist nation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bisl-sn_292-2"><a href="#cite_note-bisl-sn-292">[292]</a></sup> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism)" title="Sangha (Buddhism)">Sangha</a> having existed in a largely unbroken lineage since its introduction in the 2nd century BCE. During periods of decline, the Sri Lankan monastic lineage was revived through contact with <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ph-tbas_293-1"><a href="#cite_note-ph-tbas-293">[293]</a></sup> Buddhism is given special recognition in the Constitution which requires Sri Lankans to "protect and foster the Buddha Sasana".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the second most prevalent religion in Sri Lanka and predates Buddhism. Today, Hinduism is dominant in Northern, Eastern and Central Sri Lanka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the third most dominant religion in the country, having first been brought to the island by Arab traders over the course of many centuries, starting around the 7th century CE. Most Muslims are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> who follow the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" title="Shafi\'i">Shafi\'i</a> school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> Most followers of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Islam in Sri Lanka">Islam in Sri Lanka</a> today are believed to be descendants of those Arab traders and the local women they married.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> reached the country through Western colonists in the early 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> Around 7.4% of the Sri Lankan population are Christians, of which 82% are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholics</a> who trace their religious heritage directly to the Portuguese. Sri Lankan <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> attribute their religious heritage to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St.Francis_Xavier" title="St.Francis Xavier">St.Francis Xavier</a> as well as Portuguese missionaries. The remaining Christians are evenly split between the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ceylon" title="Church of Ceylon">Anglican Church of Ceylon</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant denominations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is also a small population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoroastrian" title="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</a> immigrants from India (<a href="/wiki/Parsis" title="Parsis">Parsis</a>) who settled in Ceylon during the period of British rule,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> but this community has steadily dwindled in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> Religion plays a prominent role in the life and culture of Sri Lankans. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> majority observe <a href="/wiki/Poya" title="Poya">Poya</a> Days each month according to the <a href="/wiki/Lunar_calendar" title="Lunar calendar">Lunar calendar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> also observe their own holidays. In a 2008 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallup_poll" title="Gallup poll">Gallup poll</a>, Sri Lanka was ranked the third most religious country in the world, with 99% of Sri Lankans saying religion was an important part of their daily life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gallu_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-gallu-302">[302]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Sri_Lanka" title="List of cities in Sri Lanka">List of cities in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<table class="navbox" width="97%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="12" style="padding:0.3em 0; line-height:1.2em; font-size:120%;">Largest cities of Sri
