Lanka">Eastern</a></td>\n<td>48,351\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Health in Sri Lanka">Health in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>Sri Lankans have a <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of 77.9 years at birth, which is 10% higher than the world average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-6"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> The infant mortality rate stands at 8.5 per 1,000 births and the maternal mortality rate at 0.39 per 1,000 births, which is on par with figures from the developed countries. The universal "pro-poor"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> health care system adopted by the country has contributed much towards these figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka ranks first among southeast Asian countries with respect to commitment of <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a>, with 33 deaths per 100,000 persons. According to  <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Department_of_Census_and_Statistics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Department of Census and Statistics (page does not exist)">Department of Census and Statistics</a>, poverty, destructive pastimes and inability to cope up with stressful situations, are the main causes behind the high suicide rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Education in Sri Lanka">Education in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="419" data-file-width="604" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg/220px-Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg/330px-Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg/440px-Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sarachchandra_Theatre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Peradeniya" title="University of Peradeniya">University of Peradeniya</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarachchandra_open-air_theatre" title="Sarachchandra open-air theatre">Sarachchandra open-air theatre</a>, named in memory of <a href="/wiki/Ediriweera_Sarachchandra" title="Ediriweera Sarachchandra">Ediriweera Sarachchandra</a>, Sri Lanka\'s premier playwright</div></div></div>\n<p>With a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of 92.5%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-7"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has one of the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literate" title="Literate">literate</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Populations" title="Populations">populations</a> amongst <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> Its youth literacy rate stands at 98%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> computer literacy rate at 35%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daynwsl_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-daynwsl-309">[309]</a></sup> and primary school enrollment rate at over 99%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> An education system which dictates 9 years of <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education" title="Compulsory education">compulsory schooling</a> for every child is in place. The <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education system</a> established in 1945,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> is a result of the initiative of <a href="/wiki/C._W._W._Kannangara" title="C. W. W. Kannangara">C. W. W. Kannangara</a> and A. Ratnayake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-312">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> It is one of the few countries in the world that provide universal free education from primary to tertiary stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kannangara led the establishment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madhya_Maha_Vidyalayas" title="Madhya Maha Vidyalayas">Madhya Maha Vidyalayas</a> (Central Schools) in different parts of the country in order to provide education to Sri Lanka\'s rural children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daynwsl_309-1"><a href="#cite_note-daynwsl-309">[309]</a></sup> In 1942 a special education committee proposed extensive reforms to establish an efficient and quality <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education system</a> for the people. However, in the 1980s changes to this system saw the separation of the administration of schools between the central government and the provincial government. Thus the elite <a href="/wiki/National_school_(Sri_Lanka)" title="National school (Sri Lanka)">National Schools</a> are controlled directly by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Sri_Lanka)" title="Ministry of Education (Sri Lanka)">Ministry of Education</a> and the provincial schools by the provincial government. Sri Lanka has approximately 9675 government schools, 817 private schools and <a href="/wiki/Pirivena" title="Pirivena">Pirivenas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-8"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sri Lanka has 15 <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public universities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> A lack of responsiveness of the education system to labour market requirements, disparities in access to quality education, lack of an effective linkage between secondary and tertiary education remain major challenges for the education sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> A number of private, degree awarding institutions have emerged in recent times to fill in these gaps, yet the participation at tertiary level education remains at 5.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> The proposed private university bill has been withdrawn by the Higher Education Ministry after university students\' heavy demonstrations and resistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Science_fiction_author" title="Science fiction author">science fiction author</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a> served as Chancellor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moratuwa_University" title="Moratuwa University">Moratuwa University</a> in Sri Lanka from 1979 to 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Transport in Sri Lanka">Transport in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>Sri Lanka has an extensive road network for inland transportation. With more than 100,000&#160;km of paved roads,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> it has one of the highest road densities in the world (1.5&#160;km of paved roads per every 1sq.km. of land). <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Expressways of Sri Lanka">E-grade</a> highways are the latest addition to Sri Lanka\'s road network. These are access-controlled, high-mobility roads with permitted speeds up to 100&#160;km/h.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> These highways connect local communities together, by-passing busy and congested town centers.\n</p><p>A and B grade roads are national (arterial) highways administered by Road Development Authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup> C and D grade roads are provincial roads coming under the purview of the Provincial Road Development Authority of the respective province. The other roads are local roads falling under local government authorities.\n</p><p>The rail network of Sri Lanka consists of main lines, coastal lines, and up-country lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> In addition, air- and water-based transportation modalities augment the inland transport of the country.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_and_media">Human rights and media</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Human rights in Sri Lanka">Human rights in Sri Lanka</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Media in Sri Lanka">Media in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Sri Lanka Broadcasting Corporation">Sri Lanka Broadcasting Corporation</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Radio_Ceylon" title="Radio Ceylon">Radio Ceylon</a>) is the oldest-running radio station in Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slbcv_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-slbcv-324">[324]</a></sup> established in 1923 by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Harper_(engineer)" title="Edward Harper (engineer)">Edward Harper</a> just three years after broadcasting began in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slbcv_324-1"><a href="#cite_note-slbcv-324">[324]</a></sup> The station broadcasts services in Sinhalese, Tamil, English and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi_language" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>. Since the 1980s, a large number of private radio stations have also been introduced. Broadcast television was introduced to the country in 1979 when the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Television_Network" title="Independent Television Network">Independent Television Network</a> was launched. Initially, all Television stations were state-controlled, but private television networks began broadcasts in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sri_Lanka&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 51 newspapers (30 Sinhala, 10 Tamil, 11 English) are published and 34 TV stations and 52 radio stations are in operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treasry_259-9"><a href="#cite_note-treasry-259">[259]</a></sup> In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a> in Sri Lanka has been alleged by media freedom groups to be amongst the <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">poorest in democratic countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> Alleged abuse of a newspaper editor by a senior government minister<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-You_are_pigs_who_eat_shit_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-You_are_pigs_who_eat_shit-327">[327]</a></sup> achieved international notoriety because of the unsolved murder of the editor\'s predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Lasantha_Wickrematunge" title="Lasantha Wickrematunge">Lasantha Wickrematunge</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Death_foretold_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-Death_foretold-328">[328]</a></sup> who had also been a critic of the government and had presaged his own death in a posthumously published article.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-written_posthumous_editorial_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-pre-written_posthumous_editorial-329">[329]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Officially, the constitution of Sri Lanka guarantees <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> as ratified by the United Nations. However, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Human rights in Sri Lanka">human rights in Sri Lanka</a> have come under criticism by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_from_Torture" title="Freedom from Torture">Freedom from Torture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_rule_in_Ceylon" title="British rule in Ceylon">British colonial rulers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> the separatist Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam (LTTE), and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Government of Sri Lanka">government of Sri Lanka</a> are accused of violating human rights. A <a href="/wiki/Report_of_the_Secretary-General%27s_Panel_of_Experts_on_Accountability_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Report of the Secretary-General\'s Panel of Experts on Accountability in Sri Lanka">report by an advisory panel to the UN secretary-general</a> has accused both the LTTE and the Sri Lankan government of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleged_war_crimes_during_the_Sri_Lankan_Civil_War" title="Alleged war crimes during the Sri Lankan Civil War">alleged war crimes</a> during final stages of the civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> Corruption remains a problem in Sri Lanka, and there is currently very little protection for those who stand up against corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> has documented <a href="/wiki/Enforced_disappearances_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Enforced disappearances in Sri Lanka">over 12,000 named individuals</a> who have undergone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enforced_disappearance" title="Enforced disappearance">disappearance</a> after detention by security forces in Sri Lanka, the second highest figure in the world since the Working Group came into being in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHRC_involuntary_disappearances_report_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNHRC_involuntary_disappearances_report-336">[336]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan government has confirmed that 6,445 of these are dead. Allegations of human rights abuses have not ended with the close of the ethnic conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-People_are_disappearing_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-People_are_disappearing-337">[337]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">UN Human Rights Commissioner</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navanethem_Pillay" title="Navanethem Pillay">Navanethem Pillay</a> visited Sri Lanka in May 2013. After her visit, she said: "The war may have ended [in Sri Lanka], but in the meantime democracy has been undermined and the rule of law eroded." Pillay spoke about the military\'s increasing involvement in civilian life and reports of military <a href="/wiki/Land_grabbing" title="Land grabbing">land grabbing</a>. She also said that, while in Sri Lanka, she had been allowed to go wherever she wanted, but that Sri Lankans who came to meet her were harassed and intimidated by security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, the UK charity <a href="/wiki/Freedom_from_Torture" title="Freedom from Torture">Freedom from Torture</a> reported that it had received 233 referrals of torture survivors from Sri Lanka for clinical treatment or other services provided by the charity. In the same year, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_from_Torture" title="Freedom from Torture">Freedom from Torture</a> published <i>Out of the Silence</i>, which documents evidence of torture in Sri Lanka and demonstrates that the practice has continued long after the end of the civil war in May 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Culture of Sri Lanka">Culture of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2010" data-file-width="2559" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG/220px-Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG/330px-Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG/440px-Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vavuniya_Kavadi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hindu devotees engaging in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavadi" title="Kavadi">Kavadi</a></i> at a temple in <a href="/wiki/Vavuniya" title="Vavuniya">Vavuniya</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The culture of Sri Lanka dates back over 2500 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> It is influenced primarily by <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-precol_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-precol-342">[342]</a></sup> Sri Lanka is the home to two main traditional cultures: the Sinhalese (centred in the ancient cities of Kandy and Anuradhapura) and the Tamil (centred in the city of Jaffna). In more recent times, the British colonial culture has also influenced the locals. Sri Lanka claims a democratic tradition matched by few other developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nub94_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-nub94-343">[343]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Tamil immigration was probably around the 3rd century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-precol_342-1"><a href="#cite_note-precol-342">[342]</a></sup> Tamils co-existed with the Sinhalese people since then, and the early mixing rendered the two ethnic groups almost physically indistinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> Ancient Sri Lanka is marked for its genius in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_constructions_of_Sri_Lanka#Irrigation_Works" title="Ancient constructions of Sri Lanka">hydraulic engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_ancient_Sri_Lanka" title="Architecture of ancient Sri Lanka">architecture</a>. The rich cultural traditions shared by all Sri Lankan cultures is the basis of the country\'s long life expectancy, advanced health standards and high literacy rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nub94_343-1"><a href="#cite_note-nub94-343">[343]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_festivals">Food and festivals</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_cuisine" title="Sri Lankan cuisine">Sri Lankan cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Festivals_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Festivals in Sri Lanka">Festivals in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SL-rice_and_curry.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SL-rice_and_curry.jpg/220px-SL-rice_and_curry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SL-rice_and_curry.jpg/330px-SL-rice_and_curry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/SL-rice_and_curry.jpg/440px-SL-rice_and_curry.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SL-rice_and_curry.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sri Lankan rice and curry</div></div></div>\n<p>Dishes include <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and curry, <a href="/wiki/Puttu" title="Puttu">pittu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiribath" title="Kiribath">kiribath</a>, wholemeal <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idiyappam" title="Idiyappam">string hoppers</a>, wattalapam (a rich pudding of Malay origin made of <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>, jaggery, <a href="/wiki/Cashew" title="Cashew">cashew nuts</a>, eggs, and spices including cinnamon and <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kottu" title="Kottu">kottu</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hopper_(food)" title="Hopper (food)">hoppers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-simplysl_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-simplysl-345">[345]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jackfruit" title="Jackfruit">Jackfruit</a> may sometimes replace rice. Traditionally food is served on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain leaf or lotus leaf</a>.\n</p><p>Middle Eastern influences and practices are found in traditional <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Moors" title="Sri Lankan Moors">Moor</a> dishes, while Dutch and Portuguese influences are found with the island\'s Burgher community preserving their culture through traditional dishes such as Lamprais (rice cooked in stock and baked in a banana leaf), Breudher (Dutch Holiday Biscuit), and Bolo Fiado (Portuguese-style layer cake).\n</p><p>In April, Sri Lankans celebrate the <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_New_Year" title="Sinhalese New Year">Buddhist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_New_Year" title="Tamil New Year">Hindu</a> new year festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dersl_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-dersl-346">[346]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esala_Perahera" title="Esala Perahera">Esala Perahera</a> is a symbolic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist_festival" title="Buddhist festival">Buddhist festival</a> consisting of dances and decorated elephants held in <a href="/wiki/Kandy" title="Kandy">Kandy</a> in July and August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esalasl_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-esalasl-347">[347]</a></sup> Fire-dances, whip-dances, Kandian dances and various other cultural dances are integral parts of the festival. Christians celebrate <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> on 25 December to celebrate the birth of Jesus Christ and <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> to celebrate the resurrection of Jesus. Tamils celebrate <a href="/wiki/Thai_Pongal" title="Thai Pongal">Thai Pongal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maha_Shivaratri" title="Maha Shivaratri">Maha Shivaratri</a>, and Muslims celebrate <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Visual.2C_literary_and_performing_arts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual,_literary_and_performing_arts">Visual, literary and performing arts</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Cinema of Sri Lanka">Cinema of Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Music of Sri Lanka">Music of Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dances_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Dances of Sri Lanka">Dances of Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Theatre of Sri Lanka">Theatre of Sri Lanka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_literature" title="Sri Lankan literature">Sri Lankan literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_(Lotus_Pond)_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG/220px-The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG/330px-The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG/440px-The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_%28Lotus_Pond%29_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_landmark_Nelum_Pokuna_(Lotus_Pond)_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Nelum_Pokuna_Mahinda_Rajapaksa_Theatre" title="Nelum Pokuna Mahinda Rajapaksa Theatre">Nelum Pokuna Mahinda Rajapaksa Theatre</a> was constructed as a major venue for the performing arts</div></div></div>\n<p>The movie <i><a href="/wiki/Kadawunu_Poronduwa" title="Kadawunu Poronduwa">Kadawunu Poronduwa</a></i> (The broken promise), produced by <a href="/wiki/S._M._Nayagam" title="S. M. Nayagam">S. M. Nayagam</a> of Chitra Kala Movietone, heralded the coming of Sri Lankan cinema in 1947. <i><a href="/wiki/Ranmuthu_Duwa" title="Ranmuthu Duwa">Ranmuthu Duwa</a></i> (Island of treasures, 1962) marked the transition cinema from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black-and-white" title="Black-and-white">black-and-white</a> to colour. It in the recent years has featured subjects such as family <a href="/wiki/Melodrama" title="Melodrama">melodrama</a>, social transformation and the years of conflict between the military and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LTTE" title="LTTE">LTTE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-easiancinem_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-easiancinem-348">[348]</a></sup> The Sri Lankan cinematic style is similar to <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> movies. In 1979, movie attendance rose to an all-time high, but has been in steady decline since then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denandind_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-denandind-349">[349]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An influential filmmaker is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lester_James_Peiris" title="Lester James Peiris">Lester James Peiris</a>, who has directed a number of movies which led to global acclaim, including <i><a href="/wiki/Rekava" title="Rekava">Rekava</a></i> (Line of destiny, 1956), <i><a href="/wiki/Gamperaliya_(film)" title="Gamperaliya (film)">Gamperaliya</a></i> (The changing village, 1964), <i><a href="/wiki/Nidhanaya" title="Nidhanaya">Nidhanaya</a></i> (The treasure, 1970) and <i><a href="/wiki/Golu_Hadawatha" title="Golu Hadawatha">Golu Hadawatha</a></i> (Cold heart, 1968).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lstjms_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-lstjms-350">[350]</a></sup> Sri Lankan-Canadian poet <a href="/wiki/Rienzi_Crusz" title="Rienzi Crusz">Rienzi Crusz</a>, is the subject of a documentary on his life in Sri Lanka. His work is published in Sinhalese and English. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">naturalized</a>-<a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ondaatje" title="Michael Ondaatje">Michael Ondaatje</a>, is well known for his English-language novels and three films.\n</p><p>The earliest music in Sri Lanka came from theatrical performances such as <i>Kolam</i>, <i>Sokari</i> and <i>Nadagam</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cambrmu_351-0"><a href="#cite_note-cambrmu-351">[351]</a></sup> Traditional music instruments such as <i>B&#233;ra</i>, <i>Thamm&#225;tama</i>, <i>Da&#365;la</i> and <i>R&#259;b&#257;n</i> were performed at these dramas. The first music album, <i>Nurthi</i>, recorded in 1903, was released through <a href="/wiki/Radio_Ceylon" title="Radio Ceylon">Radio Ceylon</a> (founded in 1925). Songwriters like <a href="/wiki/Mahagama_Sekara" title="Mahagama Sekara">Mahagama Sekara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ananda_Samarakoon" title="Ananda Samarakoon">Ananda Samarakoon</a> and musicians such as <a href="/wiki/W._D._Amaradeva" title="W. D. Amaradeva">W. D. Amaradeva</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victor_Ratnayake" title="Victor Ratnayake">Victor Ratnayake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Malini" title="Nanda Malini">Nanda Malini</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clarence_Wijewardene" title="Clarence Wijewardene">Clarence Wijewardene</a> have contributed much towards the upliftment of Sri Lankan music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmrhg_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-wmrhg-352">[352]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baila" title="Baila">Baila</a> is another popular <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">music genre</a> in the country, originated among <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Kaffirs" title="Sri Lanka Kaffirs">Kaffirs</a> or the Afro-Sinhalese community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lnlypnlu_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-lnlypnlu-353">[353]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg/220px-Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg/330px-Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg/440px-Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sri_Lanka_traditional_drum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Low Country drummer playing the traditional <i>Yak B&#233;ra</i></div></div></div>\n<p>There are three main styles of Sri Lankan classical dance. They are, the <a href="/wiki/Kandyan_dance" title="Kandyan dance">Kandyan dances</a>, low country dances and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabaragamuwa" title="Sabaragamuwa">Sabaragamuwa</a> dances. Of these, the Kandyan style, which flourished under kings of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kandy" title="Kingdom of Kandy">Kingdom of Kandy</a>, is more prominent. It is a sophisticated form of dance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dncen2_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-dncen2-354">[354]</a></sup> that consists of five sub-categories: <i>Ves dance</i>, <i>Naiyandi dance</i>, <i>Udekki dance</i>, <i>Pantheru dance</i> and <i>18 Vannam</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sldance_355-0"><a href="#cite_note-sldance-355">[355]</a></sup> An elaborate headdress is worn by the male dancers and a drum called <i>Geta B&#233;raya</i> is used to assist the dancer to keep on rhythm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_356-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-356">[356]</a></sup> In addition, four folk drama variants named <i>Sokri</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kolam" title="Kolam">Kolam</a> <i>Nadagam</i>, <i>Pasu</i>, and several devil dance variants such as <a href="/wiki/Sanni_Yakuma" title="Sanni Yakuma">Sanni Yakuma</a> and <i>Kohomba Kankariya</i> can be also observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sldance_355-1"><a href="#cite_note-sldance-355">[355]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The history of Sri Lankan painting and sculpture can be traced as far back as to the 2nd or 3rd century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lklibrform_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-lklibrform-357">[357]</a></sup> The earliest mention about the art of painting on Mahavamsa, is to the drawing of a palace on cloth using cinnabar in the 2nd century BC. The chronicles have description of various paintings in relic-chambers of Buddhist stupas, and in monastic residence.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">Theatre</a> moved into the country when a <a href="/wiki/Parsi_theatre" title="Parsi theatre">Parsi theatre</a> company from <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> introduced <i>Nurti</i>, a blend of European and Indian theatrical conventions to the Colombo audience in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sldance_355-2"><a href="#cite_note-sldance-355">[355]</a></sup> The golden age of Sri Lankan drama and theatre began with the staging of <i>Maname</i>, a play written by <a href="/wiki/Ediriweera_Sarachchandra" title="Ediriweera Sarachchandra">Ediriweera Sarachchandra</a> in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theatresl_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-theatresl-358">[358]</a></sup> It was followed by a series of popular dramas like <i>Sinhab&#257;hu</i>, <i>Pab&#257;vat&#299;</i>, <i>Mah&#257;s&#257;ra</i>, <i>Muudu Puththu</i> and <i>Subha saha Yasa</i>.\n</p><p>Sri Lankan literature spans at least two millennia, and is heir to the <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan</a> literary tradition as embodied in the hymns of the <a href="/wiki/Rigveda" title="Rigveda">Rigveda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lklinbr_359-0"><a href="#cite_note-lklinbr-359">[359]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon" title="P&#257;li Canon">P&#257;li Canon</a>, the standard collection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scripture" title="Scripture">scriptures</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> tradition, was written down in Sri Lanka during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Buddhist_council" title="Fourth Buddhist council">Fourth Buddhist council</a>, at the Alulena cave temple, <a href="/wiki/Kegalle" title="Kegalle">Kegalle</a>, as early as 29 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alulena_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-alulena-360">[360]</a></sup> Ancient chronicles such as the Mah&#257;vamsa, written in the 6th century, provide vivid descriptions of Sri Lankan dynasties. According to the German philosopher <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Geiger" title="Wilhelm Geiger">Wilhelm Geiger</a>, the chronicles are based on Sinhala <a href="/wiki/Atthakatha" title="Atthakatha">Atthakatha</a> (commentary), that dates few more centuries back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lklinbr_359-1"><a href="#cite_note-lklinbr-359">[359]</a></sup> The oldest surviving prose work is the <i>Dhampiya-Atuva-Getapadaya</i>, compiled in the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lklinbr_359-2"><a href="#cite_note-lklinbr-359">[359]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The greatest literary feats of medieval Sri Lanka include <i>Sandesha K&#257;vya</i> (poetic messages) such as <i>Gir&#257; Sandeshaya</i> (Parrot message), <i>Hansa Sandeshaya</i> (Swan message) and <i>Salalihini Sandeshaya</i> (Myna message). Poetry including <i>Kavsilumina</i>, <i>Kavya-Sekharaya</i> (diadem of poetry) and proses such as <i>Saddharma-Ratn&#257;valiya</i>, <i>Am&#257;vatura</i> (Flood of nectar) and <i>Puj&#257;valiya</i> are also notable works of this period, which is considered to be the golden age of Sri Lankan literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lklinbr_359-3"><a href="#cite_note-lklinbr-359">[359]</a></sup> The first modern-day novel, <i>Meena</i>, a work of Simon de Silva appeared in 1905,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sldance_355-3"><a href="#cite_note-sldance-355">[355]</a></sup> and was followed by a number of revolutionary literary works. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Wickramasinghe" title="Martin Wickramasinghe">Martin Wickramasinghe</a>, the author of <i><a href="/wiki/Madol_Doova" title="Madol Doova">Madol Doova</a></i> is considered the iconic figure of Sri Lankan literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martinw_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-martinw-361">[361]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Sport in Sri Lanka">Sport in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<p>While the <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a> in Sri Lanka is <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, by far the most popular sport in the country is <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-362"><a href="#cite_note-362">[362]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> also enjoys extensive popularity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-363"><a href="#cite_note-363">[363]</a></sup> as do <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football (soccer)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>. Sri Lanka\'s schools and colleges regularly organise sports and athletics teams, competing on provincial and national levels.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lanka national cricket team</a> achieved considerable success beginning in the 1990s, rising from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Underdog_(competition)" title="Underdog (competition)">underdog</a> status to winning the <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996 Cricket World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> They also won the <a href="/wiki/2014_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2014 ICC World Twenty20">2014 ICC World Twenty20</a> played in Bangladesh, beating India in the final. In addition, Sri Lanka became the runners-up of the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365">[365]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup_Final" title="2011 Cricket World Cup Final">2011</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-366"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup> and of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20" title="ICC World Twenty20">ICC World Twenty20</a> in <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2012 ICC World Twenty20">2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-367"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Former Sri Lankan <a href="/wiki/Off_spin" title="Off spin">off-spinner</a> <a href="/wiki/Muttiah_Muralitharan" title="Muttiah Muralitharan">Muttiah Muralitharan</a> has been rated as the greatest <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test match</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bowler_(cricket)" title="Bowler (cricket)">bowler</a> ever by <i><a href="/wiki/Wisden_Cricketers%27_Almanack" title="Wisden Cricketers\' Almanack">Wisden Cricketers\' Almanack</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-368"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup> and four Sri Lankan cricketers ranked 2nd (<a href="/wiki/Kumar_Sangakkara" title="Kumar Sangakkara">Sangakkara</a>), 4th (<a href="/wiki/Sanath_Jayasuriya" title="Sanath Jayasuriya">Jayasuriya</a>), 5th (<a href="/wiki/Mahela_Jayawardene" title="Mahela Jayawardene">Jayawardene</a>) and 11th (<a href="/wiki/Tillakaratne_Dilshan" title="Tillakaratne Dilshan">Dilshan</a>) highest ODI run scorers of all time, which is the second best by a team. Sri Lanka has won the <a href="/wiki/Asia_Cup" title="Asia Cup">Asia Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1986_Asia_Cup" title="1986 Asia Cup">1986</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-369"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1997_Asia_Cup" title="1997 Asia Cup">1997</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-370"><a href="#cite_note-370">[370]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2004_Asia_Cup" title="2004 Asia Cup">2004</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2008_Asia_Cup" title="2008 Asia Cup">2008</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[372]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Asia_Cup" title="2014 Asia Cup">2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-373"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> Sri Lanka once held highest team score in all three formats of cricket, where currently holds Test team total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-374"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> The country co-hosted the Cricket World Cup in <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2011 Cricket World Cup">2011</a>, and hosted the <a href="/wiki/2012_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2012 ICC World Twenty20">2012 ICC World Twenty20</a>.\n</p><p>Sri Lankans have won two medals at <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, one silver, by <a href="/wiki/Duncan_White" title="Duncan White">Duncan White</a> at <a href="/wiki/1948_Summer_Olympics" title="1948 Summer Olympics">1948 London Olympics</a> for men\'s <a href="/wiki/400_metres_hurdles" title="400 metres hurdles">400 metres hurdles</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-375"><a href="#cite_note-375">[375]</a></sup> and one silver by <a href="/wiki/Susanthika_Jayasinghe" title="Susanthika Jayasinghe">Susanthika Jayasinghe</a> at <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Sydney Olympics</a> for women\'s <a href="/wiki/200_metres" title="200 metres">200 metres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-376"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup> In 1973, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Lafir" title="Muhammad Lafir">Muhammad Lafir</a> won the <a href="/wiki/IBSF_World_Billiards_Championship" title="IBSF World Billiards Championship">World Billiards Championship</a>, the highest feat by a Sri Lankan in a <a href="/wiki/Cue_sports" title="Cue sports">Cue sport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[377]</a></sup> Sri Lanka has also won the Carrom World Championship titles twice in 2012, <a href="/wiki/2016_Carrom_World_Championship" title="2016 Carrom World Championship">2016</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-378"><a href="#cite_note-378">[378]</a></sup> and 2018, men\'s team becoming champions and women\'s team coming 2nd place. Aquatic sports such as boating, surfing, swimming, kitesurfing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-379"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> on the coast, the beaches and backwaters attract a large number of Sri Lankans and foreign tourists. There are two styles of martial arts native to Sri Lanka, <a href="/wiki/Cheena_di" title="Cheena di">Cheena di</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angampora" title="Angampora">Angampora</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_netball_team" title="Sri Lanka national netball team">Sri Lanka national netball team</a> has won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Netball_Championship" title="Asian Netball Championship">Asian Netball Championship</a> five times and are the current Asian Champions as well.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em
